Salah — Prayer

7 min
The Twelve Conditions of Jumu'ah and the Definition of Misr
Lists conditions for Jumu'ah obligation and presents intra-Hanafi definitions of misr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the twelve conditions for Jumu'ah obligation and distinguish the three Hanafi definitions of misr with their implications.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn only when twelve conditions are met; the definition of misr determines which communities can hold it.

In this passage, we explore the prerequisites for the obligation of Jumu'ah prayer. The author enumerates twelve conditions divided into personal and external, then highlights an intra-madhhab dispute over the definition of misr. Understanding this helps clarify when Jumu'ah becomes mandatory versus merely permissible.

Guided Path
1
Separate personal from external conditions
Identify which conditions pertain to the worshiper (7) and which to the external setting (5).
Personal: freedom, masculinity, puberty, residence, health, sound legs, sound eyes. External: misr, ruler, congregation, sermon, time.
2
Classify the legal function of each condition
Each condition is a shart (condition) for the obligation (luzūm) of Jumu'ah, not necessarily for its validity.
If a condition is missing, Jumu'ah is not required, but if performed it may still be valid as Zuhr?
3
Identify the contested element
The definition of misr (congregational city) is disputed among Hanafi authorities.
Three opinions are presented; the dispute is intra-Hanafi.
4
Analyze the three definitions
Compare the criteria: (1) markets, just governor, and scholar; (2) religious and general worldly needs; (3) amir and qadi who enforce penalties.
The second definition is more comprehensive; the third (from al-Hidayah) is weakened by later scholars.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify which definition is relied upon for fatwa today, citing the weakening by Ibn al-Mulaqqin and al-Nawawi.
The more inclusive definition (religious + worldly needs) is often preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* ثم شرائط لزوم الجمعة اثنا عشر :
سبعة في نفس المصلي، وهي: الحرية، والذكورة، والبلوغ،
والإقامة والصحة وسلامة الرجلين، وسلامة العينين.
وخمسةٌ في غير المصلي: المصر، والسلطان، والجماعة، والخطبة،
والوقت.
واختلفوا في صفة المصر:
قال بعضهم: هو كل بلد فيها أسواق، ووال يُنصف المظلوم من الظالم، وعالم يُرجع إليه في الحوادث.
وقال بعضهم: هو أن يوجد فيه حوائج الدين، وعامة حوائج الدنيا، فحوائج الدين: القاضي والمفتي، وحوائج الدنيا: أن يعيش فيها كل صانع بصناعته من السنة إلى السنة.
وفي «الهداية»: هو كلُّ موضع له أمير وقاض ينفذ الأحكام، ويُقيم
الحدود.
وضعفه ابن الملقن في البدر المنير ۳۷۷/۱۱ ، والنووي في المجموع ٤٨٨/٤.
* Then the conditions for the obligation of Friday prayer are twelve:
Seven concerning the worshiper himself: freedom, masculinity, puberty, residence, health, soundness of both legs, and soundness of both eyes.
And five concerning other than the worshiper: the congregational city, the ruler, the congregation, the sermon, and the time.
And they differed regarding the description of the city:
Some said: It is any town in which there are markets, a governor who does justice to the oppressed against the oppressor, and a scholar who is consulted on incidents.
And some said: It is that religious needs and most worldly needs are found in it. The religious needs: the judge and the mufti. The worldly needs: that every craftsman can live through his craft from year to year.
And in al-Hidāyah: It is every place that has an amīr and a qāḍī who execute the rulings and establish the penalties.
And Ibn al-Mulaqqin in al-Badr al-Munīr 11/377 and al-Nawawī in al-Majmū' 4/488 weakened it.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage enumerates the twelve conditions (sharā'iṭ) for the obligation (luzūm) of Jumu'ah prayer and then discusses the definition of 'miṣr' (city) among Hanafi scholars. The conditions are divided into seven personal and five external. Personal conditions: freedom (not a slave), masculinity (not female), puberty (not a child), residence (not a traveler), health (not sick), soundness of legs (not unable to walk), and soundness of eyes (not blind). External conditions: a congregational city (miṣr), a ruler (sulṭān) or his deputy, a congregation (jamā'ah) of at least three besides the imam, the sermon (khuṭbah), and the time (of Zuhr on Friday). The passage then notes disagreement (ikhtilāf) among Hanafi authorities on the precise definition of 'miṣr'. Three opinions are presented: (1) it has markets, a just governor, and a scholar; (2) it contains religious needs (a judge and mufti) and general worldly needs such that every artisan can sustain himself year-round; (3) from al-Hidāyah: it has an amir and a qadi who enforce legal rulings and establish penal punishments. The latter definition is weakened by later scholars Ibn al-Mulaqqin and al-Nawawi. This ikhtilaf is intra-Hanafi; the operative definition for fatwa is typically the more comprehensive one.

Key Terms
شرائط لزوم الجمعة (sharā'iṭ luzūm al-Jumu'ah): Conditions that make Jumu'ah prayer obligatory on a person; if any are missing, Jumu'ah is not required of that person.
مصر (miṣr): A major settlement with sufficient infrastructure and governance to support Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one personal condition for Jumu'ah to be obligatory?
A) Being a traveler
B) Being blind
C) Soundness of both legs
D) Being a minor

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is obligatory only when all twelve conditions are fulfilled; the precise definition of a city (misr) is debated among Hanafi scholars, with the more inclusive definition being preferred for fatwa.

Conditions for Jumu'ah and the Definition of a City (Misr)
Listing conditions for obligatory Jumu'ah and defining Misr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the twelve conditions for the obligation of Jumu'ah and explain the Hanafi definitions of a city (misr) that satisfy the external condition.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only obligatory when twelve conditions are met — seven within the person and five external, including a valid city.

Friday prayer is a weekly obligation upon qualified Muslims, but it is not required of everyone in all circumstances. This passage from Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyira lays out the twelve conditions that must be present for Jumu'ah to become binding (luzum). It also delves into differing Hanafi views on what constitutes a 'misr' (city) — a crucial external condition. Understanding these conditions helps you recognize who must attend Jumu'ah and where it can be validly held.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of conditions
The author divides conditions into those relating to the person (7) and those external (5). Note which conditions are personal capacities (e.g., free, male, adult, resident, healthy, sound limbs) and which are communal/institutional (city, ruler, congregation, sermon, time).
Personal conditions exclude those who are not independent or able.
2
Analyze the personal conditions
Each of the seven conditions excludes certain individuals: slaves, women, children, travellers, the sick, the blind, and the lame. Reflect on the wisdom behind each.
Women are exempt due to domestic responsibilities; children are not yet mukallaf.
3
Examine the external conditions
The five external conditions require an established Islamic community with leadership and infrastructure. Pay special attention to 'misr' (city) as it is further defined.
These conditions ensure Jumu'ah is a public, organized act of worship.
4
Study the definitions of misr
The text presents multiple Hanafi definitions: one emphasizing markets, a just ruler, and a scholar; another including judge, mufti, and self-sufficiency; and the Hidayah's requirement of a governor and judge. Consider how these definitions affect the obligation.
Narrower definitions limit where Jumu'ah is obligatory.
5
Note the critique of the Hidayah definition
The author mentions that Ibn al-Mulaqqin and al-Nawawi weakened the Hidayah definition. Reflect on the consequences of a narrower vs. broader definition.
Later scholars preferred a more inclusive understanding for facilitation.

Source Text

باب صلاة الجمعة
أو في مصلى المصر.
* قوله : (أو في مصلى المصر)؛ لأن له حكم المصر.
- وليس الحكم مقصوراً على المصلى، بل تجوز في جميع أفنية المصر، وقدروه بمنتهى حد الصوت، والأذان.
* ثم شرائط لزوم الجمعة اثنا عشر :
سبعة في نفس المصلي، وهي: الحرية، والذكورة، والبلوغ،
والإقامة والصحة وسلامة الرجلين، وسلامة العينين.
وخمسةٌ في غير المصلي: المصر، والسلطان، والجماعة، والخطبة،

وقال بعضهم: هو أن يوجد فيه حوائج الدين، وعامة حوائج الدنيا، فحوائج الدين: القاضي والمفتي، وحوائج الدنيا: أن يعيش فيها كل صانع بصناعته من السنة إلى السنة.

.٨٢/١ (١)
Chapter on Friday Prayer
Or in the musalla (prayer area) of the city.
* His statement: (Or in the musalla of the city); because it has the same ruling as the city.
- The ruling is not restricted to the musalla, rather it is permitted in all open spaces of the city, and they estimated it by the limit of the range of the voice and the call to prayer.
* Then the conditions for the obligation of Friday are twelve:
Seven are in the person himself: freedom, masculinity, adulthood,
residence, health, soundness of both legs, and soundness of both eyes.
And five are external to the person: the city, the ruler, the congregation, the sermon,
and the time.
And they differed regarding the description of the city (misr):
Some said: It is every town in which there are markets, a ruler who helps the oppressed against the oppressor, and a scholar to whom one refers in events.
And some said: It is that in which are found the needs of the religion and the general needs of the world; the needs of the religion: the judge and the mufti; the needs of the world: that every craftsman can live by his craft from year to year.
And in Al-Hidayah: It is every place that has a governor and a judge who implement rulings and establish
limits.
And Ibn Al-Mulaqqin in Al-Badr Al-Munir 11/377, and Al-Nawawi in Al-Majmu' 4/488 weakened it.
(1) 1/82.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyira, a commentary on Mukhtasar Al-Quduri, opens the chapter on Friday prayer. It begins by clarifying the location for Jumu'ah: it can be performed in the musalla or any open area within the city, as long as it is within earshot of the adhan. Then it lists the twelve conditions for the obligation of Jumu'ah, dividing them into seven relating to the individual (freedom, male, adult, resident, healthy, sound legs, sound eyes) and five external conditions (a city, a ruler, a congregation, a sermon, and the prescribed time). The commentary then discusses the definition of 'misr' (city/town) for the purpose of Jumu'ah. Several definitions are presented: a place with markets, a just ruler, and a scholar; or a place where both religious needs (judge, mufti) and worldly needs (sustenance for craftsmen) are met. The Hidayah defines it as a place with a governor and a judge who enforce laws and punishments. The author notes that later scholars like Ibn Al-Mulaqqin and Al-Nawawi weakened this definition. This discussion establishes the minimal requirements for a settlement to be considered a city for Jumu'ah obligations.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A city or town with amenities such as markets, a ruler, a judge, and scholars, sufficient for religious and worldly needs.
شرائط (shurat): Conditions that must be present for Jumu'ah to be obligatory.
لزوم (luzum): Obligation or binding necessity; here it refers to the conditions that make Jumu'ah obligatory on an individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Freedom
B) Masculinity
C) Adulthood
D) Wealth

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is only obligatory when twelve conditions are met; the definition of a city is critical for determining where it must be performed.

Obligation of Jumu'ah for Those Outside the City
Inter-madhhab dispute on obligation based on city boundaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person outside the city regarding Jumu'ah and explain the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The city boundary severs obligation for Jumu'ah — even hearing the adhan does not bind you.

This passage first addresses a person outside the city: is Jumu'ah obligatory? The Hanafi school says no, because the city's ruling ends at its boundary, analogous to a traveler shortening prayers. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that hearing the call obligates. Understanding this difference clarifies the role of physical boundaries in defining obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The person is outside the city boundaries, not a resident. The question is whether they must enter the city for Jumu'ah.
2
State the Hanafi position
It is not obligatory to enter the city for Jumu'ah. The text says: 'لا يجب عليه دخول المصر للجمعة'.
This applies even if they hear the adhan.
3
Trace the Hanafi proof
The proof is an analogy: if such a person were a traveler, they would shorten prayers at that location. This shows the city's ruling (hukm al-misr) is severed at its boundaries.
The text uses 'ألا ترى' to present this analogy.
4
Note the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hearing the call to prayer obligates Jumu'ah, regardless of location.
The opposing dalil is based on the general command to attend when called.
5
Identify the practical difference
Per Hanafi, such a person may stay and pray Dhuhr. Per Shafi'i, they must attend Jumu'ah or sin.
This difference affects those living near city boundaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن أبي يوسف إذا اجتمعوا في أكبر مساجدهم: لم يسعهم. ومن كان خارج المصر: لا يجب عليه دخول المصر للجمعة؛ لانفصاله عن المصر، ألا ترى أنه لو خرج مسافراً، وبلغ ذلك المكان: قَصَر؛ لانقطاع حكم المصر.
(1)
وقال الشافعي: يجب عليه إذا [سمع] النداء.
والقروي إذا دخل المصرَ يوم الجمعة: إن نوى أن يمكث يومه ذلك: لزمته الجمعة، وإن نوى أن يخرج قبل دخول الوقت أو بعده: فلا جمعة عليه. كذا في الوجيز.
ولا بأس أن يُجمِّع الناس في المصر في موضعين، ولا يجوز في أكثر من ذلك(٢).
وعن أبي يوسف: لا تجوز في موضعين إلا أن يكون بين الجامعين نهر عظيم.
وإن لم يكن : فالجمعة لمَن سَبَقَ ، وعلى الآخرين إعادة الظهر. وإن صلوا معاً، ولا يُدرى من سبق: لا تجوز صلاتهم جميعاً.
(1) مغني المحتاج ٢٧٧/١.
(۲) قال في الدر المختار ٢٨/٥ - ٢٩ مع ابن عابدين ط دمشق): وتُودَّى في مصر واحد بمواضع كثيرة مطلقاً، على المذهب، وعليه الفتوى. اهـ، ووافقه ابن عابدين، ونقل ما يؤكد ذلك.
And from Abu Yusuf: If they gather in their largest mosque and it does not accommodate them. And whoever is outside the city: it is not obligatory upon him to enter the city for Friday; because he is separated from the city. Do you not see that if he left as a traveler and reached that place, he shortens the prayer, due to the severance of the ruling of the city.
(1)
And Al-Shafi'i said: It is obligatory upon him when he hears the call to prayer.
And the villager if he enters the city on Friday: if he intends to stay that day, Friday becomes obligatory upon him; and if he intends to leave before the entrance of the time or after it, then there is no Friday upon him. Thus in Al-Wajiz.
And there is no harm if people gather for Friday in two locations in the city, and it is not permissible in more than that (2).
And from Abu Yusuf: It is not permissible in two locations unless there is a great river between the two gatherings.
And if there is not, then Friday is for the one who preceded, and upon the others is the repetition of Dhuhr. And if they pray together and it is not known who preceded, their prayer is not valid at all.
(1) Mughni al-Muhtaj 1/277.
(2) He said in Al-Durr al-Mukhtar (5/28-29 with Ibn Abidin, Damascus edition): It is performed in one city in many places absolutely, according to the madhhab, and upon it is the fatwa. End quote, and Ibn Abidin agreed and transmitted what confirms that.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on Friday prayer with several rulings. First, from Abu Yusuf: if the largest mosque is insufficient, the obligation remains on those who can find space. A person outside the city (even within hearing distance) is not obligated to enter for Jumu'ah, as the city's jurisdiction ends at its boundaries. This is supported by the analogy that such a person shortens prayers if they are a traveler. Then the Shafi'i position is mentioned: according to Imam al-Shafi'i, the obligation applies to those within hearing of the adhan, even outside the city. The Hanafi position differs, as clarified earlier. Next, the ruling for a villager (قروي) who enters the city on Friday: if he intends to stay the whole day, Jumu'ah becomes obligatory on him; if he intends to leave before or after the time, it does not. This is from the book 'Al-Wajiz'. Finally, the discussion on multiple Jumu'ah congregations in one city: according to the earlier Hanafi position, it is permissible in two locations but not more than two, unless there is a large river separating them. Abu Yusuf restricts it to one location unless separated by a river. If they pray simultaneously and precedence is unknown, all prayers are invalid and must be repeated as Dhuhr. The commentator adds a note from later Hanafi texts (Al-Durr al-Mukhtar) that the fatwa is that multiple locations are absolutely permitted.

Key Terms
قصر (qasr): Shortening of prayers from four rak'ahs to two while traveling.
انقطاع حكم المصر (inqita' hukm al-misr): The severance of the city's legal rulings, e.g., for prayer shortening and Jumu'ah obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the Hanafi proof for not obligating Jumu'ah on a person outside the city?
A) The person is not a resident of the city
B) The person would shorten prayers if traveling to that location
C) The person cannot hear the adhan clearly
D) The person has an excuse of travel

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school conditions Jumu'ah obligation on being within the city's jurisdiction, not on hearing the call.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Ruling for a Villager Entering the City on Friday
Ruling statement on villager's obligation based on intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling for a villager entering the city on Friday based on his intention.

Core Idea
A villager's Jumu'ah obligation hinges on intention to stay the full day.

The passage then discusses a villager (qarawi) who enters the city on Friday. The ruling depends on his intention: if he intends to stay the whole day, Jumu'ah is obligatory; if he intends to leave before or after the time, it is not. This ruling is from Al-Wajiz and clarifies how temporary presence affects obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The subject is a villager (qarawi) who is not a resident of the city but enters it on Friday.
The villager is considered a traveler unless he intends to stay.
2
Consider intention to stay the full day
If he intends to remain in the city for the entire day of Friday, Jumu'ah becomes obligatory upon him.
Staying the full day makes him like a resident for that day.
3
Consider intention to leave before or after time
If he intends to leave before the time of Jumu'ah enters or after it, then Jumu'ah is not obligatory upon him.
Leaving before the time means he avoids obligation; leaving after means he may have already prayed Dhuhr?
4
Apply to a scenario
Example: A villager enters the city at 10 AM Friday, intending to visit and return home by 2 PM. Jumu'ah time is 1 PM. Since he intends to leave after Jumu'ah time (2 PM > 1 PM), he is obligated? Actually need to check: before time or after. The text says 'before the entrance of the time or after it'. If he intends to leave after the time, which is ambiguous: does he stay through the time? He might be present during the time. The ruling says if he intends to leave after the time, then no Jumu'ah upon him. That seems to indicate that if he intends to leave after the time but before the day ends? We need to interpret. The text: 'إن نوى أن يخرج قبل دخول الوقت أو بعده: فلا جمعة عليه.' So both before and after the time, no obligation. This means if he intends to leave at any point during the day, whether before or after the Jumu'ah time, he is not obligated. But what if he stays through the prayer? The condition is his intention at entry. So if he intends to leave after the time, he is not obligated even though he might actually be present during the prayer. This is a lenient ruling.

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on Friday prayer with several rulings. First, from Abu Yusuf: if the largest mosque is insufficient, the obligation remains on those who can find space. A person outside the city (even within hearing distance) is not obligated to enter for Jumu'ah, as the city's jurisdiction ends at its boundaries. This is supported by the analogy that such a person shortens prayers if they are a traveler. Then the Shafi'i position is mentioned: according to Imam al-Shafi'i, the obligation applies to those within hearing of the adhan, even outside the city. The Hanafi position differs, as clarified earlier. Next, the ruling for a villager (قروي) who enters the city on Friday: if he intends to stay the whole day, Jumu'ah becomes obligatory on him; if he intends to leave before or after the time, it does not. This is from the book 'Al-Wajiz'. Finally, the discussion on multiple Jumu'ah congregations in one city: according to the earlier Hanafi position, it is permissible in two locations but not more than two, unless there is a large river separating them. Abu Yusuf restricts it to one location unless separated by a river. If they pray simultaneously and precedence is unknown, all prayers are invalid and must be repeated as Dhuhr. The commentator adds a note from later Hanafi texts (Al-Durr al-Mukhtar) that the fatwa is that multiple locations are absolutely permitted.

Key Terms
قروي (qarawi): A villager or someone from a rural area who is not a resident of the city.
يمكث يومه (yamkuth yawmah): To stay the entire day from dawn to sunset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling for a villager who enters the city on Friday intending to leave after Jumu'ah time?
A) Jumu'ah is obligatory
B) Jumu'ah is not obligatory
C) He must pray both Jumu'ah and Dhuhr
D) He should pray Dhuhr only if he misses Jumu'ah

Key Takeaway
A villager's Jumu'ah obligation is determined solely by his intention at entry: staying the full day obligates; leaving (before or after time) exempts.

Multiple Jumu'ah Congregations in One City
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute and later fatwa on multiple Jumu'ah locations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on multiple Jumu'ah congregations in one city, the intra-Hanafi dispute, and the later fatwa.

Core Idea
Multiple Jumu'ah prayers: allowed in two locations unless a river separates; later fatwa permits absolutely.

The passage concludes with rulings on holding Jumu'ah in more than one location in a city. The earlier Hanafi position permits two locations, but not more. Abu Yusuf restricts it to one unless a large river separates them. If two congregations pray simultaneously and precedence is unknown, both are invalid. Later Hanafi fatwa (Al-Durr al-Mukhtar) permits multiple locations absolutely. This shows the evolution of the school's position over time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
The text says: 'There is no harm in two locations, and it is not permissible in more than that.' This is the earlier Hanafi position allowing exactly two Jumu'ah congregations in one city.
This ruling assumes the city is not too large; two locations are sufficient for need.
2
Note Abu Yusuf's restriction
Abu Yusuf holds that even two locations are not allowed unless separated by a large river. If no river, only one Jumu'ah is valid.
The river acts as a natural barrier, making the two groups effectively in separate jurisdictions.
3
Understand the rule if two congregations occur
If there is no river and two groups pray simultaneously, the one that started first is valid; the others must repeat Dhuhr. If it is unknown who preceded, all prayers are invalid.
This emphasizes the importance of precedence when multiple congregations occur without proper separation.
4
Recognize the later fatwa
The commentator notes that in Al-Durr al-Mukhtar, the fatwa has shifted: it is absolutely permissible to have multiple Jumu'ah prayers in many locations in one city.
This reflects changing circumstances: larger cities with dispersed populations made it impractical to have only one or two Jumu'ah gatherings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن أبي يوسف إذا اجتمعوا في أكبر مساجدهم: لم يسعهم. ومن كان خارج المصر: لا يجب عليه دخول المصر للجمعة؛ لانفصاله عن المصر، ألا ترى أنه لو خرج مسافراً، وبلغ ذلك المكان: قَصَر؛ لانقطاع حكم المصر.
(1)
وقال الشافعي: يجب عليه إذا [سمع] النداء.
والقروي إذا دخل المصرَ يوم الجمعة: إن نوى أن يمكث يومه ذلك: لزمته الجمعة، وإن نوى أن يخرج قبل دخول الوقت أو بعده: فلا جمعة عليه. كذا في الوجيز.
ولا بأس أن يُجمِّع الناس في المصر في موضعين، ولا يجوز في أكثر من ذلك(٢).
وعن أبي يوسف: لا تجوز في موضعين إلا أن يكون بين الجامعين نهر عظيم.
وإن لم يكن : فالجمعة لمَن سَبَقَ ، وعلى الآخرين إعادة الظهر. وإن صلوا معاً، ولا يُدرى من سبق: لا تجوز صلاتهم جميعاً.
(1) مغني المحتاج ٢٧٧/١.
(۲) قال في الدر المختار ٢٨/٥ - ٢٩ مع ابن عابدين ط دمشق): وتُودَّى في مصر واحد بمواضع كثيرة مطلقاً، على المذهب، وعليه الفتوى. اهـ، ووافقه ابن عابدين، ونقل ما يؤكد ذلك.
And from Abu Yusuf: If they gather in their largest mosque and it does not accommodate them. And whoever is outside the city: it is not obligatory upon him to enter the city for Friday; because he is separated from the city. Do you not see that if he left as a traveler and reached that place, he shortens the prayer, due to the severance of the ruling of the city.
(1)
And Al-Shafi'i said: It is obligatory upon him when he hears the call to prayer.
And the villager if he enters the city on Friday: if he intends to stay that day, Friday becomes obligatory upon him; and if he intends to leave before the entrance of the time or after it, then there is no Friday upon him. Thus in Al-Wajiz.
And there is no harm if people gather for Friday in two locations in the city, and it is not permissible in more than that (2).
And from Abu Yusuf: It is not permissible in two locations unless there is a great river between the two gatherings.
And if there is not, then Friday is for the one who preceded, and upon the others is the repetition of Dhuhr. And if they pray together and it is not known who preceded, their prayer is not valid at all.
(1) Mughni al-Muhtaj 1/277.
(2) He said in Al-Durr al-Mukhtar (5/28-29 with Ibn Abidin, Damascus edition): It is performed in one city in many places absolutely, according to the madhhab, and upon it is the fatwa. End quote, and Ibn Abidin agreed and transmitted what confirms that.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on Friday prayer with several rulings. First, from Abu Yusuf: if the largest mosque is insufficient, the obligation remains on those who can find space. A person outside the city (even within hearing distance) is not obligated to enter for Jumu'ah, as the city's jurisdiction ends at its boundaries. This is supported by the analogy that such a person shortens prayers if they are a traveler. Then the Shafi'i position is mentioned: according to Imam al-Shafi'i, the obligation applies to those within hearing of the adhan, even outside the city. The Hanafi position differs, as clarified earlier. Next, the ruling for a villager (قروي) who enters the city on Friday: if he intends to stay the whole day, Jumu'ah becomes obligatory on him; if he intends to leave before or after the time, it does not. This is from the book 'Al-Wajiz'. Finally, the discussion on multiple Jumu'ah congregations in one city: according to the earlier Hanafi position, it is permissible in two locations but not more than two, unless there is a large river separating them. Abu Yusuf restricts it to one location unless separated by a river. If they pray simultaneously and precedence is unknown, all prayers are invalid and must be repeated as Dhuhr. The commentator adds a note from later Hanafi texts (Al-Durr al-Mukhtar) that the fatwa is that multiple locations are absolutely permitted.

Key Terms
جامعين (jami'ayn): Two congregations or groups performing Jumu'ah simultaneously in different locations.
نهر عظيم (nahr 'azim): A large river that physically separates two locations, considered a barrier for the purpose of Jumu'ah validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only one
B) Two
C) One unless a river separates
D) Multiple, absolutely

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on multiple Jumu'ah congregations evolved from a restriction of two to absolute permissibility, reflecting the principle of tahawwul al-fatwa.

The Obligation of Jumu'ah for Those Outside the City: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on Jumu'ah obligation outside the city

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that Jumu'ah is not obligatory for those outside the city and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The ruling of the city ends at its boundary; beyond it, the obligation of Jumu'ah drops like the traveler's prayer shortens.

This lesson examines a key disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the obligation of Friday prayer on a person who is outside the city limits. The Hanafi school, represented by Abu Yusuf, draws an analogy with the traveler's prayer, while al-Shafi'i relies on the general call to prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the Hanafi position (no obligation) and the Shafi'i position (obligation upon hearing the call). Note the source: Abu Yusuf for Hanafi, al-Shafi'i for the opposing view.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof (qiyas)
The Hanafi school uses qiyas on the traveler who shortens prayer beyond the city. The illa is the separation from the city's ruling (inqita' hukm al-misr).
The text says 'ala tara annahu law kharaja musafiran... qasara' — do you not see that if he traveled he would shorten.
3
Identify the Shafi'i proof
Al-Shafi'i makes it obligatory upon hearing the call to prayer (al-nida'), regardless of location relative to the city.
The text mentions 'wajaba 'alayhi idha sami'a al-nida'.
4
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: a person outside the city is not required to enter for Jumu'ah in the Hanafi school, whereas the Shafi'i requires it if he hears the call.
This affects daily practice for residents just outside city limits.

Chapter of Friday Prayer. And according to Muhammad: It is permissible in two and three places. And from Abu Hanifa: It is permissible only in one place. And it is not disliked to set out for travel on Friday before noon and after it. And Malik said: It is disliked when the sun has passed the zenith. His saying: (And it is not permissible in villages). If you say: This has been known from his saying: It is not permissible except in a city mosque, so what is the need for what he mentioned? It is said: This is emphasis, and emphasis has come in the Qur'an: Allah says: 'And establish weight with justice' (al-Rahman 9), then He said: 'And do not cheat in the weight' (al-Rahman 9), and this was already known by His saying: 'And establish weight with justice'. His saying: (And its establishment is not permissible except for the sultan) because it is established with a great gathering, and dispute may occur in advancement, giving precedence, and other things, i.e., advancement between the imams, and giving precedence among the congregation, and other things, i.e., regarding the place where the prayer is performed. (1) See for other views in the school: Hashiyat Ibn Abidin 5/86. (2) Imam Khalil text in al-Mukhtasar p.98 (with Jawahir al-Iklil) on the prohibition of travel for one upon whom Friday is obligatory at noon.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah covers several key rulings on Friday prayer (Salat al-Jumu'ah) within the Hanafi school. It begins with a ruling from Abu Yusuf: if a city's largest mosque cannot accommodate all residents, it is not obligatory for those outside the city to enter for Friday prayer. This is analogized to a traveler who shortens prayer beyond city limits. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, making it obligatory upon hearing the call. The text next addresses a villager entering the city: if he intends to stay the entire day, Jumu'ah is obligatory; otherwise not. The passage then discusses multiple Jumu'ah congregations in one city. The relied-upon Hanafi position (as per al-Durr al-Mukhtar) allows many locations absolutely, but the text presents a range of views: Abu Yusuf requires a river between congregations, while Muhammad and Abu Hanifa differ on the number. The ruling on villages is emphatically repeated—Jumu'ah is invalid in villages. Its establishment is restricted to the sultan or his deputy to avoid disputes. Regarding travel, the Hanafi position is that it is not disliked before or after noon, contra Malik who dislikes it after zawal. The commentary justifies the repetition of the village prohibition by analogy with Quranic emphasis. The leadership condition is explained by the need to prevent conflicts in a large gathering.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A large city or metropolis that qualifies for holding Friday prayer due to population and infrastructure.
انقطاع حكم المصر (inqita' hukm al-misr): The cutting off of the city's ruling at its boundary, meaning that obligations tied to the city (like full prayer or Jumu'ah) cease beyond it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary evidence for not obligating Jumu'ah on a person outside the city?
A) Quranic verse
B) Hadith
C) Qiyas on the traveler
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
The obligation of Jumu'ah is tied to the city; outside it, the ruling is cut off, akin to the traveler's prayer.

The Villager's Intention: Determining Jumu'ah Obligation
Ruling on villager's obligation based on intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on a villager's obligation for Jumu'ah based on his intention to stay or leave the city.

Core Idea
A villager's intention to stay the entire day triggers Jumu'ah; leaving before the time absolves him.

This lesson focuses on a specific rule regarding a villager (qarawi) who enters a city on Friday. The Hanafi school makes the obligation of Jumu'ah contingent on the villager's intention: if he intends to stay the whole day, he must pray Jumu'ah; if he intends to leave before or after the time enters, he is free to pray Zuhr instead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and scenario
The subject is a villager (qarawi) who enters the city on Friday. The scenario is when he enters before the time of Jumu'ah.
2
Distinguish between two intentions
If he intends to stay the entire day (i.e., remains until after Jumu'ah), Jumu'ah becomes obligatory upon him. If he intends to leave before the time enters or after it (but before completing Jumu'ah), he is not obligated.
The text says 'in nawa an yamkutha yawmahu dhalika: lazimatihi al-jumu'ah'.
3
Understand the legal basis
The ruling is based on the principle that Jumu'ah is not obligatory on a villager unless he becomes a 'resident' for the day. His intention to stay makes him effectively a resident for Friday.
4
Apply the ruling
If he is uncertain whether he will stay, or if he changes his intention, the safe approach is to pray Jumu'ah to avoid missing it.
The text does not cover uncertainty; this is a practical extension.

And if there is not, then Friday prayer is for the one who preceded, and upon the others is the repetition of Zuhr. And if they prayed together and it is not known who preceded, their prayer is all invalid. (1) Mughni al-Muhtaj 1/277. (2) Said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar 5/28-29 with Ibn Abidin (Damascus edition): It is performed in one city in many places absolutely, according to the school, and upon it is the fatwa. End. And Ibn Abidin agreed and transmitted what confirms that. [PAGE_024] 24. And it is not permissible in villages. And its establishment is not permissible except for the sultan. Chapter of Friday Prayer. And according to Muhammad: It is permissible in two and three places. And from Abu Hanifa: It is permissible only in one place. And it is not disliked to set out for travel on Friday before noon and after it. And Malik said: It is disliked when the sun has passed the zenith. His saying: (And it is not permissible in villages). If you say: This has been known from his saying: It is not permissible except in a city mosque, so what is the need for what he mentioned? It is said: This is emphasis, and emphasis has come in the Qur'an: Allah says: 'And establish weight with justice' (al-Rahman 9), then He said: 'And do not cheat in the weight' (al-Rahman 9), and this was already known by His saying: 'And establish weight with justice'. His saying: (And its establishment is not permissible except for the sultan) because it is established with a great gathering, and dispute may occur in advancement, giving precedence, and other things, i.e., advancement between the imams, and giving precedence among the congregation, and other things, i.e., regarding the place where the prayer is performed. (1) See for other views in the school: Hashiyat Ibn Abidin 5/86. (2) Imam Khalil text in al-Mukhtasar p.98 (with Jawahir al-Iklil) on the prohibition of travel for one upon whom Friday is obligatory at noon.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah covers several key rulings on Friday prayer (Salat al-Jumu'ah) within the Hanafi school. It begins with a ruling from Abu Yusuf: if a city's largest mosque cannot accommodate all residents, it is not obligatory for those outside the city to enter for Friday prayer. This is analogized to a traveler who shortens prayer beyond city limits. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, making it obligatory upon hearing the call. The text next addresses a villager entering the city: if he intends to stay the entire day, Jumu'ah is obligatory; otherwise not. The passage then discusses multiple Jumu'ah congregations in one city. The relied-upon Hanafi position (as per al-Durr al-Mukhtar) allows many locations absolutely, but the text presents a range of views: Abu Yusuf requires a river between congregations, while Muhammad and Abu Hanifa differ on the number. The ruling on villages is emphatically repeated—Jumu'ah is invalid in villages. Its establishment is restricted to the sultan or his deputy to avoid disputes. Regarding travel, the Hanafi position is that it is not disliked before or after noon, contra Malik who dislikes it after zawal. The commentary justifies the repetition of the village prohibition by analogy with Quranic emphasis. The leadership condition is explained by the need to prevent conflicts in a large gathering.

Key Terms
قروي (qarawi): A villager, i.e., a person from a village (qarya) where Jumu'ah is not established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a villager become obligated to pray Jumu'ah upon entering a city on Friday?
A) If he intends to stay the entire day
B) If he hears the adhan
C) If he enters before noon
D) Always

Key Takeaway
A villager's obligation for Jumu'ah hinges on his intention to remain in the city the whole day.

Multiple Friday Congregations in One City: Internal Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on number of Jumu'ah locations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Hanafi positions on the permissibility of multiple Jumu'ah congregations in one city and state the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Hanafi imams differed on multiple Jumu'ah; later fatwa allows many locations absolutely.

This lesson explores the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the number of Friday prayers that may be held in a single city. The matn initially states two places are permissible without harm, but more than two is not. However, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Abu Hanifa each had different views, and later Hanafi fatwa (as per al-Durr al-Mukhtar) allows many locations absolutely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
The base text (al-Quduri) states: 'no harm in two places, not permissible in more than that.'
This is the default statement in the matn.
2
List the three imams' positions
Abu Yusuf: two places are allowed only if a great river separates them; otherwise one is valid. Muhammad: two or three places are allowed. Abu Hanifa: only one place is allowed.
These are reported in the commentary.
3
Note the later fatwa
Al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Ibn Abidin state that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that multiple places are allowed absolutely, regardless of number.
This overrides the earlier restrictions.
4
Understand the rationale for the restriction
The restriction stems from the desire to avoid disunity and disputes about precedence. The sultan or his deputy typically designates one location.
The commentary explains potential disputes in advancement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الجمعة
وعن أبي يوسف إذا اجتمعوا في أكبر مساجدهم: لم يسعهم. ومن كان خارج المصر: لا يجب عليه دخول المصر للجمعة؛ لانفصاله عن المصر، ألا ترى أنه لو خرج مسافراً، وبلغ ذلك المكان: قَصَر؛ لانقطاع حكم المصر.
(1)
وقال الشافعي: يجب عليه إذا النداء. سمع
والقروي إذا دخل المصرَ يوم الجمعة: إن نوى أن يمكث يومه ذلك: لزمته الجمعة، وإن نوى أن يخرج قبل دخول الوقت أو بعده: فلا جمعة عليه. كذا في الوجيز».
ولا بأس أن يُجمِّع الناس في المصر في موضعين، ولا يجوز في أكثر من ذلك(٢).
وعن أبي يوسف: لا تجوز في موضعين إلا أن يكون بين الجامعين نهر عظيم.
وإن لم يكن : فالجمعة لمَن سَبَقَ ، وعلى الآخرين إعادة الظهر. وإن صلوا معاً، ولا يُدرى من سبق: لا تجوز صلاتهم جميعاً.
(1) مغني المحتاج ٢٧٧/١.
(۲) قال في الدر المختار ٢٨/٥ - ٢٩ مع ابن عابدين ط دمشق): وتُودَّى في مصر واحد بمواضع كثيرة مطلقاً، على المذهب، وعليه الفتوى. اهـ، ووافقه ابن عابدين، ونقل ما يؤكد ذلك.

٢٤
ولا تجوز في القُرَى.
ولا تجوز إقامتها إلا للسلطان،
باب صلاة الجمعة
وعند محمد : تجوز في موضعين وثلاثة.
وعن أبي حنيفة : لا تجوز إلا في موضع واحد.
ولا يكره الخروج إلى السفر يوم الجمعة قبل الزوال، وبعده).
وقال مالك (۲) : يكره إذا زالت الشمس.
قوله: (ولا تجوز في القرى).
فإن قلت: قد عُرف هذا بقوله : لا تجوز إلا في مصر جامع، فما الحاجة إلى ما ذكره؟
قيل: هذا تأكيد، وقد جاء التأكيد في القرآن: قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَقِيمُوا الْوَزْنَ بِالْقِسْطِ . الرحمن /۹ ، ثم قال: ﴿وَلَا تُخسِرُوا الْمِيزَانَ ) ، وقد علم هذا بقوله: ﴿ وَأَقِيمُوا الْوَزْنَ بِالْقِسْطِ .
قوله: (ولا تجوز إقامتها إلا للسلطان)؛ لأنها تُقام بجمع عظيم، وقد تقع المنازعة في التقدم، والتقديم، وغير ذلك، أي في التقدم بين الإمامين، والتقديم بين الجماعة، وغير ذلك، أي في الموضع الذي يُصلى
(1) ينظر لأقوال أخرى في المذهب : حاشية ابن عابدين ٨٦/٥.
(۲) نص الإمام خليل في المختصر ص۹۸ (مع جواهر الإكليل) على حرمة سفر من تلزمه الجمعة بالزوال.
Chapter of Friday Prayer. And from Abu Yusuf: If they gather in their largest mosque and it does not accommodate them. And whoever is outside the city (misr): it is not obligatory upon him to enter the city for Friday prayer because he is separated from the city. Do you not see that if he set out as a traveler and reached that place, he shortens (the prayer) because the ruling of the city is cut off. (1) And al-Shafi'i said: It is obligatory upon him if he hears the call. And the villager who enters the city on Friday: if he intends to stay that day, Friday prayer becomes obligatory upon him; and if he intends to leave before the time enters or after it, then no Friday prayer is upon him. Thus in al-Wajiz. And there is no harm in people praying Friday in the city in two places, and it is not permissible in more than that. (2) And from Abu Yusuf: It is not permissible in two places unless there is a great river between the two congregations. And if there is not, then Friday prayer is for the one who preceded, and upon the others is the repetition of Zuhr. And if they prayed together and it is not known who preceded, their prayer is all invalid. (1) Mughni al-Muhtaj 1/277. (2) Said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar 5/28-29 with Ibn Abidin (Damascus edition): It is performed in one city in many places absolutely, according to the school, and upon it is the fatwa. End. And Ibn Abidin agreed and transmitted what confirms that. [PAGE_024] 24. And it is not permissible in villages. And its establishment is not permissible except for the sultan. And it is not disliked to set out for travel on Friday before noon and after it. And Malik said: It is disliked when the sun has passed the zenith. (2) Imam Khalil text in al-Mukhtasar p.98 (with Jawahir al-Iklil) on the prohibition of travel for one upon whom Friday is obligatory at noon.

Travel on Friday: Hanafi vs Maliki Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on traveling on Friday

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on traveling on Friday and compare it with the Maliki position.

Core Idea
Hanafis permit travel on Friday at any time; Malikis prohibit it after zawal.

This lesson covers a minor ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding travel on Friday. The Hanafi school holds that it is not disliked (la yukrah) to travel before or after noon, while Malik considers it disliked after the sun passes the zenith (zawal).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Travel on Friday is not disliked at any time, whether before zawal or after it.
2
State the Maliki position
Malik holds that travel after zawal is disliked (yukrah).
The dislike may be tahrimi according to some Maliki sources.
3
Understand the basis
Hanafis focus on the absence of a clear prohibition; Malikis consider that after zawal the obligation of Jumu'ah becomes imminent for residents.
4
Determine the practical consequence
For Hanafis, a traveler may leave before or after noon without any sin; for Malikis, he should delay travel until after Jumu'ah if he is obligated.

The Authority to Establish Jumu'ah: The Sultan's Permission
Ruling on the authority to establish Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school restricts the establishment of Jumu'ah to the sultan or his deputy.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires sultanic permission to avoid disputes over leadership and precedence.

This lesson addresses a procedural requirement: the Friday prayer should only be established by the ruler (sultan) or his authorized representative. The rationale given is to prevent conflicts that may arise over leadership (imamah) and precedence in a large gathering.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states: 'Its establishment is not permissible except for the sultan'.
2
Understand the wisdom (hikma)
Jumu'ah involves a large gathering. Disputes can occur about who leads, who stands where, and other organizational matters. The sultan's authority prevents such disputes.
The commentary mentions 'manaza'a fi al-taqaddum wa al-taqdim'.
3
Note the application
In the absence of a sultan, his deputy or a qadi may authorize someone. In modern times, the government or mosque authority is considered the deputy.
4
Distinguish from necessity
If the sultan does not appoint anyone, the community may choose an imam, but it is better to have official authorization.
This is not in the immediate text but is a standard Hanafi extension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الجمعة
وعن أبي يوسف إذا اجتمعوا في أكبر مساجدهم: لم يسعهم. ومن كان خارج المصر: لا يجب عليه دخول المصر للجمعة؛ لانفصاله عن المصر، ألا ترى أنه لو خرج مسافراً، وبلغ ذلك المكان: قَصَر؛ لانقطاع حكم المصر.
(1)
وقال الشافعي: يجب عليه إذا النداء. سمع
والقروي إذا دخل المصرَ يوم الجمعة: إن نوى أن يمكث يومه ذلك: لزمته الجمعة، وإن نوى أن يخرج قبل دخول الوقت أو بعده: فلا جمعة عليه. كذا في الوجيز».
ولا بأس أن يُجمِّع الناس في المصر في موضعين، ولا يجوز في أكثر من ذلك(٢).
وعن أبي يوسف: لا تجوز في موضعين إلا أن يكون بين الجامعين نهر عظيم.
وإن لم يكن : فالجمعة لمَن سَبَقَ ، وعلى الآخرين إعادة الظهر. وإن صلوا معاً، ولا يُدرى من سبق: لا تجوز صلاتهم جميعاً.
(1) مغني المحتاج ٢٧٧/١.

(1) ينظر لأقوال أخرى في المذهب : حاشية ابن عابدين ٨٦/٥.
(۲) نص الإمام خليل في المختصر ص۹۸ (مع جواهر الإكليل) على حرمة سفر من تلزمه الجمعة بالزوال.
Chapter of Friday Prayer. And from Abu Yusuf: If they gather in their largest mosque and it does not accommodate them. And whoever is outside the city (misr): it is not obligatory upon him to enter the city for Friday prayer because he is separated from the city. Do you not see that if he set out as a traveler and reached that place, he shortens (the prayer) because the ruling of the city is cut off. (1) And al-Shafi'i said: It is obligatory upon him if he hears the call. And the villager who enters the city on Friday: if he intends to stay that day, Friday prayer becomes obligatory upon him; and if he intends to leave before the time enters or after it, then no Friday prayer is upon him. Thus in al-Wajiz. And there is no harm in people praying Friday in the city in two places, and it is not permissible in more than that. (2) And from Abu Yusuf: It is not permissible in two places unless there is a great river between the two congregations. And if there is not, then Friday prayer is for the one who preceded, and upon the others is the repetition of Zuhr. And if they prayed together and it is not known who preceded, their prayer is all invalid. (1) Mughni al-Muhtaj 1/277. (2) Said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar 5/28-29 with Ibn Abidin (Damascus edition): It is performed in one city in many places absolutely, according to the school, and upon it is the fatwa. End. And Ibn Abidin agreed and transmitted what confirms that. [PAGE_024] 24. And it is not permissible in villages. And its establishment is not permissible except for the sultan. Chapter of Friday Prayer. And according to Muhammad: It is permissible in two and three places. And from Abu Hanifa: It is permissible only in one place. And it is not disliked to set out for travel on Friday before noon and after it. And Malik said: It is disliked when the sun has passed the zenith. His saying: (And it is not permissible in villages). If you say: This has been known from his saying: It is not permissible except in a city mosque, so what is the need for what he mentioned? It is said: This is emphasis, and emphasis has come in the Qur'an: Allah says: 'And establish weight with justice' (al-Rahman 9), then He said: 'And do not cheat in the weight' (al-Rahman 9), and this was already known by His saying: 'And establish weight with justice'. His saying: (And its establishment is not permissible except for the sultan) because it is established with a great gathering, and dispute may occur in advancement, giving precedence, and other things, i.e., advancement between the imams, and giving precedence among the congregation, and other things, i.e., regarding the place where the prayer is performed. (1) See for other views in the school: Hashiyat Ibn Abidin 5/86. (2) Imam Khalil text in al-Mukhtasar p.98 (with Jawahir al-Iklil) on the prohibition of travel for one upon whom Friday is obligatory at noon.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah covers several key rulings on Friday prayer (Salat al-Jumu'ah) within the Hanafi school. It begins with a ruling from Abu Yusuf: if a city's largest mosque cannot accommodate all residents, it is not obligatory for those outside the city to enter for Friday prayer. This is analogized to a traveler who shortens prayer beyond city limits. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, making it obligatory upon hearing the call. The text next addresses a villager entering the city: if he intends to stay the entire day, Jumu'ah is obligatory; otherwise not. The passage then discusses multiple Jumu'ah congregations in one city. The relied-upon Hanafi position (as per al-Durr al-Mukhtar) allows many locations absolutely, but the text presents a range of views: Abu Yusuf requires a river between congregations, while Muhammad and Abu Hanifa differ on the number. The ruling on villages is emphatically repeated—Jumu'ah is invalid in villages. Its establishment is restricted to the sultan or his deputy to avoid disputes. Regarding travel, the Hanafi position is that it is not disliked before or after noon, contra Malik who dislikes it after zawal. The commentary justifies the repetition of the village prohibition by analogy with Quranic emphasis. The leadership condition is explained by the need to prevent conflicts in a large gathering.

Key Terms
سلطان (sultan): The ruler or his deputy who authorizes the establishment of Friday prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ruling on Traveling Before Friday Prayer
States that traveling before noon on Friday is not disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on traveling on Friday before and after zawal, and evaluate the Maliki counter-position.

Core Idea
Traveling on Friday is not disliked in the Hanafi school, even after zawal.

When is it permissible to travel on Friday? A simple question with a subtle difference between schools. This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah presents the Hanafi position clearly: it is not disliked to travel before or after zawal. Yet Imam Malik disagrees regarding after zawal. Understanding this difference illuminates how each school views the imminence of the Friday obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the Hanafi statement: 'ولا يكره الخروج إلى السفر يوم الجمعة قبل الزوال، وبعده.' What is the legal ruling for traveling on Friday, both before and after zawal?
The ruling is that it is NOT makruh (disliked).
2
Note the opposing view
The text then cites Imam Malik: 'وقال مالك: يكره إذا زالت الشمس.' What is the Maliki ruling and when does it apply?
Malik considers it makruh after zawal.
3
Understand the point of difference
The disagreement hinges on whether the obligation of Friday prayer becomes binding immediately upon zawal. Hanafi holds that for a traveler, the obligation is not yet personal, so travel remains permissible. Maliki holds that zawal makes the prayer time enter, so travel becomes disliked.
4
Apply the practical consequence
Consider a traveler leaving after zawal. For a Hanafi, no problem. For a Maliki, it would be makruh. This is the thamarah al-khilaf—the fruit of the disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يكره الخروج إلى السفر يوم الجمعة قبل الزوال، وبعده). وقال مالك : يكره إذا زالت الشمس.
And it is not disliked to set out for travel on Friday before noon and after it. And Malik said: it is disliked when the sun has passed the meridian.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on traveling on Friday. The Hanafi position is that it is not disliked (makruh) to travel before zawal (noon) or after it. However, Imam Malik holds that after zawal it becomes makruh because the time for Friday prayer has entered and the obligation is imminent. The difference arises from whether the obligation of Friday prayer is considered binding immediately upon zawal or only after the prayer actually begins. The Hanafi view is that traveling is permissible as long as one is not already obligated to attend, which is not the case for a traveler who has not yet intended residence. The text simply states the positions without further proof.

Key Terms
الزوال (al-zawāl): The moment when the sun passes the meridian, marking the beginning of the time for Zuhr and Friday prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it disliked to travel on Friday after noon (zawal)?
A) Yes, it is makruh.
B) No, it is not disliked.
C) It is haram.
D) Only before zawal it is allowed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling is that traveling on Friday is not disliked at any time, contrary to the Maliki view.

Friday Prayer Conditions: City and Sultan's Permission
Ruling with proof on city and sultan conditions for Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for Friday prayer in the Hanafi school (city and sultan's permission) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on multiple locations.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is invalid in villages and requires sultan's authority to prevent dispute.

This lesson examines two foundational conditions for Friday prayer in the Hanafi school: the requirement that it be held in a large city (miṣr jāmiʿ) and the necessity of the sultan's permission. The passage also discusses an intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the number of locations within a city where Friday can be validly performed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Friday prayer is the act. The passage states it is not valid in villages (condition 1) and not valid except with sultan (condition 2). So the ruling is that these conditions are necessary for validity.
The ruling is batil (invalid) if conditions are not met.
2
Locate the dalil
The author provides a rational proof (dalil aqli) for the sultan condition: large gathering leads to disputes; sultan prevents fitna. For the village condition, the author offers an analogy to Quranic emphasis (verse on weight) to show that the repeated statement is emphasis, not a new ruling.
The main proof is rational reasoning for sultan's condition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For sultan: the rational reason (cause) is that Friday requires a large gathering, which can cause disputes over leadership, timing, etc. The sultan's authority resolves these issues, thus the condition is necessary.
This is a maslaha-based proof.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa says only one location per city; Muhammad says two or three locations are valid.
The text does not resolve this dispute.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text does not specify a preferred view. Later Hanafi practice generally follows Abu Hanifa's one-location view under normal circumstances.
The mufta bihi is often Abu Hanifa's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

From Abu Hanifa: it is not valid except in one place. His saying: (And it is not valid in villages). If you say: This has been known by his saying: it is not valid except in a congregational city mosque, so what is the need for what he mentioned? It is said: This is emphasis, and emphasis has come in the Quran: Allah said: 'And establish the weight with justice' (55:9), then said: 'And do not cheat the balance', and this was known by His saying: 'And establish the weight with justice'. His saying: (And its establishment is not valid except for the sultan); because it is held with a large gathering, and dispute may occur about precedence and advancement and other things, i.e., precedence between imams, and advancement among the congregation, and other things, i.e., the place where it is prayed, and the performance at the beginning and end of the time, and the appointment of the khatib. And because some people may precede to the mosque and hold it for their own purpose, and it is missed by others, so its command is given to the sultan because he is most likely to calm fitna and bring equality among them. Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Friday prayer by stating two conditions: (1) Friday prayer is not valid in villages (qurā), only in a large city (misr jāmiʿ) where a congregational mosque exists. The author clarifies that the mention of 'villages' is an emphasis, as the previous statement 'only in a congregational city' already implies this. He analogizes to Quranic repetition of 'establish weight' followed by 'do not cheat' for emphasis. (2) The establishment of Friday prayer is only valid by the sultan (or his delegate, like a governor or judge) because Friday requires a large gathering and disputes may arise over who leads, where to pray, and timing. Delegating authority to the sultan prevents fitna and ensures fairness. Additionally, an intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned: Imam Muhammad allows Friday prayer in two or three locations within a city, while Abu Hanifa strictly permits only one location. The text does not resolve this dispute here, but the relied-upon position in the later Hanafi school is often Abu Hanifa's view (one location).

Key Terms
القرى (al-qurā): Villages or rural areas that are not considered large cities (amṣār).
السلطان (al-sulṭān): The ruler or his authorized delegate (amīr, qāḍī) who has authority over the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is valid only with the sultan's permission.
D) It is valid but makruh.

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer in the Hanafi school is only valid in a large city and with the sultan's permission; the number of permissible locations is disputed within the school.

Time Condition for Friday Prayer and Ruling on Expiry
Sets time condition for Friday prayer and rules on expiration during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Friday prayer time expiry and explain the qiyas proof that distinguishes Friday from Zuhr.

Core Idea
If Friday prayer time expires, it becomes invalid; must pray Zuhr anew — building is not allowed.

This passage addresses a critical timing condition for Friday prayer: it must be performed within the Zuhr time window. If the prayer extends beyond that window, the Hanafi school holds that the Friday prayer is nullified and a full Zuhr prayer must be offered from the beginning. The Maliki school dissents, allowing the worshipper to continue the same prayer as Zuhr. The debate hinges on whether the difference in recitation (jahr vs sirr) prevents 'building' one prayer upon another.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its consequence
Recognize that the time of Zuhr is a condition (shart) for Friday prayer. If the time expires during the prayer, the Friday prayer becomes invalid.
The text says 'fatasih fi waqt al-zuhr, wa la tasih ba'dahu'.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi ruling is that you must start Zuhr anew (istaqbala al-zuhr); you do not build (la yabni) the Friday prayer into Zuhr.
The verb 'yabni' is key: building means continuing the same prayer with a changed intention.
3
Identify the opposing Maliki position
Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) holds that one does build (yabni) – i.e., continue the prayer as Zuhr without restarting.
The Maliki proof is not given in the text; it is based on the idea that both prayers occupy the same time slot.
4
Follow the Hanafi qiyas proof
The Hanafi proof is an analogy (qiyas) to the case of Fajr and Zuhr: if Fajr time ends and Zuhr enters, you cannot build Zuhr upon Fajr because recitation differs. Similarly, Friday (jahr) and Zuhr (sirr) differ, so building is impermissible.
The illa (effective cause) is the difference in loudness of recitation.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
A Hanafi must pray a complete new four-rak'ah Zuhr with silent recitation. A Maliki can continue the two rak'ahs with the intention of Zuhr and recite silently from where he left off.
This difference affects actual practice in the mosque.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن شرائطها : الوقتُ، فتصح في وقت الظهر، ولا تصح بعده. حتى لو خرج الوقتُ وهو فيها استقبل الظهر، ولا يبني الظهر على الجمعة؛ لأنهما مختلفان. وعند مالك : يبني. لنا: أنهما صلاتان يُجهر في إحداهما بالقراءة، ولا يُجهر في الأخرى: فلا يجوز بناء إحداهما على الأخرى، كالفجر والظهر.
And among its conditions: time, so it is valid in the time of Zuhr, and not valid after it. So if the time exits while he is in it, he starts Zuhr anew, and does not build Zuhr upon Friday because they are different. According to Malik: he builds. Our proof: they are two prayers, one is recited aloud and the other silently, so it is not permissible to build one upon the other, like Fajr and Zuhr.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage establishes the time condition for Friday prayer: it must be performed within the time of Zuhr (from zawal until the length of an object's shadow equals twice its height, per the Hanafi school). If the time expires while one is still engaged in the Friday prayer (e.g., because the prayer was prolonged), the Friday prayer becomes invalid. The person must then pray Zuhr from the beginning. He may not simply continue the prayer as Zuhr (building) because the two prayers are different in nature. The Maliki school disagrees and allows building (continuing as Zuhr). The Hanafi proof is an analogy (qiyas) to the case of Fajr and Zuhr: if someone starts Fajr (which is recited aloud) and the time of Zuhr enters, he cannot build Zuhr upon it because recitation differs. Similarly, Friday is recited aloud while Zuhr is silent, so building is impermissible.

Key Terms
بني (يبني) (banā (yabnī)): To build one prayer upon another, i.e., to continue the same prayer sequence and count it as a different prayer after the time changes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Complete the prayer as Zuhr.
B) Stop the prayer and pray Zuhr later.
C) Start Zuhr from the beginning (استقبل الظهر).
D) Repeat Friday prayer after the time.

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is only valid within Zuhr time; if time expires during prayer, it becomes batil and must be restarted as Zuhr from the beginning.

Conditions of the Friday Khutbah
Conditions of the Friday khutbah as a condition of prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions of the Friday khutbah and explain why its absence invalidates the Friday prayer.

Core Idea
The Friday khutbah must be after zawal and before men; otherwise the prayer fails.

The Friday sermon (khutbah) is not merely a tradition but a legal condition for the validity of the Friday prayer. This passage from a classical Hanafi text specifies two essential conditions for the khutbah itself: timing and audience. Understanding these conditions helps ensure the prayer is performed correctly according to the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling: khutbah as a condition
The passage says 'min sharā’iṭihā al-khuṭbah qabla al-ṣalāh' — the khutbah is among the conditions of Friday prayer. Recognize that this makes the khutbah a prerequisite (shart), not a recommended act. Without it, the prayer is invalid.
Conditions are external requirements; here the khutbah is a condition, not a pillar (rukn) of the prayer itself.
2
Recall the first condition: timing after zawal
The text states 'an takūna ba‘da al-zawāl' — the khutbah must occur after zawal (the sun's zenith). Zawal marks the beginning of the Friday prayer time. If the khutbah is delivered before, it is invalid, regardless of when the prayer is performed.
Zawal is when the sun begins to decline; this is the start of the zuhr/Friday time.
3
Recall the second condition: presence of men
The text states 'bi-ḥaḍrati al-rijāl' — in the presence of men. The majority of Hanafi scholars interpret this as the presence of at least three men besides the imam (the minimum for Friday prayer). Women and children alone are insufficient.
This condition links to the obligation of Friday prayer on adult free men; the khutbah addresses them.
4
Understand the consequence of missing a condition
If either condition is not met, the khutbah is invalid. Since the khutbah is a condition of the Friday prayer, the Friday prayer itself becomes invalid and must be offered as zuhr instead.
The ruling is from the Hanafi school; other schools may differ on the status of the khutbah.
5
Memorize for application
This passage is a memorization anchor. Commit to memory: 'Sharṭā al-khuṭbah: ba‘da al-zawāl, bi-ḥaḍrati al-rijāl.' This will serve in both study and practice.
Use flashcards or repetition to internalize.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن شرائطها: الخطبة قبل الصلاة. ثم للخطبة شرطان: أحدهما: أن تكون بعد الزوال. والثاني: بحضرة الرجال.
And among its conditions: the khutbah before the prayer. Then for the khutbah there are two conditions: one: that it be after zawal. And the second: in the presence of men.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage adds another condition for Friday prayer: it must be preceded by a sermon (khutbah). The khutbah itself has two sub-conditions: (1) It must take place after zawal (i.e., after the time for Friday has entered). (2) It must be delivered in the presence of men (meaning at least the minimum number required for Friday prayer, typically three men besides the imam according to some Hanafi views). If these conditions are not met, the Friday prayer is not valid. This is a straightforward ruling without further proof.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khuṭbah): The sermon delivered before Friday prayer, consisting of two parts with a sitting in between.
بحضرة الرجال (bi-ḥaḍrati al-rijāl): In the presence of men (i.e., at least a group of men sufficient for the validity of Friday prayer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when must the khutbah of Friday prayer be delivered?
A) Before zawal.
B) After zawal.
C) After the prayer.
D) At any time of Friday.

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah must occur after zawal and in the presence of men; otherwise the Friday prayer is invalid.

Time as a Condition for Jumu'ah Prayer
States the time condition for Jumu'ah and refutes Maliki view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time condition for Jumu'ah according to the Hanafi school and explain why Zuhr cannot be built upon Jumu'ah using qiyas.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only valid in Zuhr time; if time expires, you must pray Zuhr separately—you cannot 'build' Zuhr on Jumu'ah.

This lesson examines a key condition for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer: its time. The Hanafi school insists that Jumu'ah must be performed within the Zuhr time window. If the Zuhr time ends while one is still praying Jumu'ah, the prayer becomes void. The passage also refutes the Maliki view that allows building Zuhr upon the interrupted Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and ruling
The text states that time (waqt) is a condition (shart) for Jumu'ah. Determine the ruling: Jumu'ah is valid only in the time of Zuhr.
The condition is external to the prayer itself.
2
Understand the consequence of time expiry
If Zuhr time exits while one is performing Jumu'ah, the Jumu'ah becomes invalid. The person must face (i.e., intend and pray) Zuhr from the beginning.
No building (bina') is allowed.
3
State the Maliki alternative
Imam Malik holds that one can build Zuhr upon the incomplete Jumu'ah (continue as Zuhr without restarting). Recognize the point of disagreement.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the Hanafi qiyas
The Hanafi proof uses analogy: Jumu'ah and Zuhr differ in recitation (jahar vs sirr), just like Fajr and Zuhr. Since building is not allowed between Fajr and Zuhr, it is not allowed between Jumu'ah and Zuhr.
The illa is the difference in recitation mode.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن شرائطها : الوقتُ، فتصح في وقت الظهر، ولا تصح بعده.  قوله : (ومن شرائطها الوقت، فتصح في وقت الظهر، ولا تصح بعده)، حتى لو خرج الوقتُ وهو فيها استقبل الظهر، ولا يبني الظهر على الجمعة؛ لأنهما مختلفان. وعند مالك : يبني. لنا: أنهما صلاتان يُجهر في إحداهما بالقراءة، ولا يُجهر في الأخرى: فلا يجوز بناء إحداهما على الأخرى، كالفجر والظهر.
And among its conditions: the time, so it is valid in the time of Zuhr, and is not valid after it. He said: (And among its conditions: the time, so it is valid in the time of Zuhr, and is not valid after it), such that if the time exits while he is in it, he turns to Zuhr, and does not build Zuhr upon Jumu'ah because they are different. According to Malik: he builds. For us: they are two prayers in one of which the recitation is aloud, and in the other it is not aloud: so it is not permissible to build one upon the other, like Fajr and Zuhr.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on the time condition for Jumu'ah prayer. It states that the time for Jumu'ah is the same as Zuhr, and if the Zuhr time expires while one is performing Jumu'ah, that Jumu'ah becomes invalid and one must pray Zuhr anew. The author then addresses a differing view from Imam Malik, who held that one can build Zuhr upon Jumu'ah (i.e., complete it as Zuhr). The Hanafi response uses an analogy (qiyas): Jumu'ah is recited aloud, Zuhr silently, so they are as different as Fajr and Zuhr, and building is not permitted.

Key Terms
الوقت (al-waqt): The time period for Zuhr prayer, which is also the time for Jumu'ah.
بناء (bina'): Legal building: connecting a subsequent act to a prior one, such as completing an interrupted prayer as another prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if the Zuhr time expires while one is still in the Jumu'ah prayer?
A) Complete the Jumu'ah prayer as it is.
B) Stop and pray Zuhr immediately without repetition.
C) Pray Zuhr from the beginning; do not build on the Jumu'ah.
D) Combine the two prayers.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah must be performed strictly within Zuhr time; if time expires, the prayer is void and must be repeated as Zuhr separately—building is not allowed.

The Sitting Between the Two Khutbahs: A Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Dispute on khutbah conditions between Hanafi and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the sitting between the two Jumu'ah khutbahs, explain why it is not a condition, and contrast it with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
The sitting between the two khutbahs is for rest, not a condition—Hanafis prioritize ease over strict form.

The Jumu'ah khutbah is a condition for the Friday prayer, but its details vary between schools. In this passage, we explore the Hanafi view on two disputed elements: the recitation of Qur'an and the sitting between the two khutbahs. Understanding these differences helps clarify when a Jumu'ah is valid and when it must be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions of the khutbah
From the passage, list the conditions: the khutbah must be before the prayer, after zawal, and consist of two parts separated by a sitting. Note that the sitting itself is considered a condition by some.
The passage also mentions the length: about a surah from the long mufassal.
2
Distinguish the two disputes
Separate the dispute on Qur'an recitation (Hanafi: sunnah; Shafi'i: wajib) from the dispute on the sitting (Hanafi: not a condition; Shafi'i: condition). Focus on the latter.
Both disputes are inter-madhhab.
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof for the sitting
The passage states the sitting is for rest (istiraah) and not a condition. Consider why a rest is not essential: the khutbah itself is the core, and a brief pause is only recommended.
The Hanafi position relies on the idea of ease (taysir) in worship.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i view
According to the Shafi'i school, the sitting is a condition, so one continuous khutbah would invalidate the Jumu'ah. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: practical consequence.
This affects whether the prayer needs to be repeated if the sitting is omitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن شرائطها : الخطبة قبل الصلاة.  يخطب الإمامُ خُطبتين يَفْصِلُ بينهما بقعدة . ولو خطب بعد الصلاة، أو قبل الزوال: لا تجوز الجمعة.  ومقدارهما : مقدار سورة من طوال المفصل. ومقدار ما يقرأ فيها من القرآن ثلاث آيات قصار، أو آية طويلة. وقراءة القرآن في الخطبة: سنة عندنا. وقال الشافعي: واجبة.  ومقدار الجلوس بينهما عند الطحاوي: مقدار ما يَمَس موضعَ جلوسه من المنبر. وفي ظاهر الرواية : مقدار ثلاث آيات. كذا في «الفتاوى». قال في «النهاية»: وهذه القعدة عندنا للاستراحة، وليست بشرط. وعند الشافعي: شرط. حتى لا يُكتفى عنده بالخطبة الواحدة وإن طالت. - قال الخُجَندي: السُّنَّة في الخُطبة أن يحمد الله، ويُثني عليه، ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ويعظ الناس، ويقرأ القرآن.
And among its conditions: the khutbah before the prayer. The Imam delivers two khutbahs, separating them with a sitting. If he gives the khutbah after the prayer, or before zawal (noon), the Jumu'ah is not valid. Their length is the length of a surah from the long mufassal. The amount of what he recites from the Qur'an in them is three short verses, or one long verse. Recitation of the Qur'an in the khutbah: is sunnah according to us. And al-Shafi'i said: obligatory. The amount of the sitting between them according to al-Tahawi: the amount to touch his sitting place on the minbar. And in al-Zahir al-Riwayah: the amount of three verses. Thus in al-Fatawa. He said in al-Nihayah: this sitting according to us is for rest, and is not a condition. According to al-Shafi'i: it is a condition, so that according to him one khutbah is not sufficient even if long. - al-Khujandi said: the sunnah in the khutbah is to praise Allah, glorify Him, send blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him), exhort the people, and recite the Qur'an.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the conditions of the Jumu'ah khutbah. It first states that the khutbah must be before the prayer; if after or before zawal, it is invalid. The khutbah consists of two parts with a sitting between. The recommended length is a surah from the long mufassal, and the Qur'an recitation is three short verses or one long verse. On the ruling of Qur'an recitation in the khutbah, the Hanafi school considers it sunnah, while Imam al-Shafi'i considers it obligatory (wajib). On the sitting between the two khutbahs, the Hanafi school (in the relied-upon position) holds that it is for rest and not a condition, while Shafi'i considers it a condition. The passage then lists the recommended content of the khutbah according to al-Khujandi.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered by the imam before the Jumu'ah prayer, consisting of two parts.
القعدة (al-qa'dah): The sitting between the two khutbahs.
السنة (al-sunnah): Recommended, not obligatory. Here used for recitation of Qur'an in the khutbah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a condition (shart) for validity.
B) It is for rest (istiraah) and not a condition.
C) It is wajib (obligatory) but not a condition.
D) It is forbidden if done intentionally.

Key Takeaway
The sitting between the two khutbahs is not a condition for Jumu'ah according to Hanafis; it is only a rest, so omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.
