The Basic Structure of the Friday Khutbah: Two Sermons and the Sitting
Explains rulings of Friday khutbah, its conditions, and internal Hanafi disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement for the Friday khutbah to consist of two sermons separated by a sitting, and identify the conditions related to timing and measure.

Core Idea
The Friday khutbah is a condition for Jumu'ah: two sermons with a sitting between; if given after prayer or before noon, the prayer is invalid.

This lesson introduces the foundational structure of the Friday khutbah as established by the Hanafi school. The passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar states clearly that the imam delivers two sermons separated by a sitting. We will analyze the measure of the sermons, the timing restrictions, and the nature of the sitting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Friday khutbah. It is a condition (shart) for the validity of Friday prayer, not a pillar.
If the khutbah is omitted, the Friday prayer is invalid.
2
Locate the basic requirement
The matn states: 'يخطب الإمام خطبتين يفصل بينهما بقعدة' (The Imam delivers two sermons, separating them with a sitting).
This is the core structure.
3
Note the timing conditions
The khutbah must be delivered after noon (zawal) and before the prayer. If given after prayer or before noon, Jumu'ah is invalid.
Timing is a condition for validity.
4
Examine the measure of the sermons
The passage gives the measure as a surah from the long Mufassal, and the recitation of Quran as three short verses or one long verse.
This is the recommended length, not obligatory.
5
Understand the sitting
The sitting between sermons is for rest, not a condition (shart). This is the Hanafi position, contrasting with al-Shafi'i.
The passage cites al-Nihaya: 'هذه القعدة عندنا للاستراحة، وليست بشرط'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الجمعة - يخطب الإمامُ خُطبتين يَفْصِلُ بينهما بقعدة . ولو خطب بعد الصلاة، أو قبل الزوال: لا تجوز الجمعة. قوله : (يخطب الإمام خطبتين يفصل بينهما بقعدة). ومقدارهما : مقدار سورة من طوال المفصل. ومقدار ما يقرأ فيها من القرآن ثلاث آيات قصار، أو آية طويلة. وقراءة القرآن في الخطبة: سنة عندنا. وقال الشافعي: واجبة. ومقدار الجلوس بينهما عند الطحاوي: مقدار ما يَمَس موضعَ جلوسه من المنبر. وفي ظاهر الرواية : مقدار ثلاث آيات. كذا في «الفتاوى». قال في «النهاية»: وهذه القعدة عندنا للاستراحة، وليست بشرط. وعند الشافعي: شرط. حتى لا يُكتفى عنده بالخطبة الواحدة وإن طالت. - قال الخُجَندي: السُّنَّة في الخُطبة أن يحمد الله، ويُثني عليه، ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ويعظ الناس، ويقرأ القرآن، ويخطب قائماً على طهارة . فإن اقتصر على ذكر الله تعالى : جاز عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا بد من ذِكْرٍ طويل يُسمى خُطبة. وإن خطب قاعداً، أو على غير طهارة : جاز، ويكره . ويدعو للمؤمنين والمؤمنات، ويكون الجهرُ فى الخطبة الثانية دون الأولى. * قوله : (ويخطب قائماً على طهارة)؛ لأن القيام فيها متوارث. وروي أن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه سئل عن ذلك، فقال للسائل: ألست تتلو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَتَرَكُوكَ فَأَيما. الجمعة / ١١ . * قوله: (فإن اقتصر على ذكر الله تعالى: جاز عند أبي حنيفة)؛ لقوله تعالى: (فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ ). الجمعة ٩ ، ولم يفصل. وهذا إذا كان على قصد الخطبة، أما إذا عطس، فحمد الله، أو سبح، أو هلل متعجباً من شيء: فإنه لا ينوب عن الخطبة، إجماعاً. * قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد لا بد من ذكرٍ طويل يسمى خطبة)، وأدناه من قوله : التحيات لله إلى... قوله: عبده ورسوله؛ لأن الخطبة هي الواجبة، والتسبيح: لا يسمى خطبة. قوله: (وإن خطب قاعداً ، أو على غير طهارة: جاز)؛ لحصول المقصود، وهو الذكر والوعظ، (إلا) أنه يكره) ؛ لما فيه من الفصل بينهما وبين الصلاة.
Chapter of Friday Prayer - The Imam delivers two sermons, separating them with a sitting. If he gives the sermon after the prayer, or before noon, the Friday prayer is not valid. His statement: (The Imam delivers two sermons, separating them with a sitting). Their measure: the measure of a surah from the long ones of Mufassal. And the measure of what is recited in it of Quran is three short verses, or one long verse. And recitation of Quran in the sermon: is Sunnah according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: obligatory. The measure of the sitting between them according to al-Tahawi: the measure of what touches his sitting place from the minbar. And in the apparent narration: the measure of three verses. Likewise in al-Fatawa. He said in al-Nihaya: This sitting according to us is for rest, and it is not a condition. According to al-Shafi'i: it is a condition. Such that one sermon is not sufficient for him even if long. Al-Khujandi said: The Sunnah in the sermon is to praise Allah, extol Him, send blessings on the Prophet (SAW), admonish the people, recite Quran, and give the sermon standing with purity. If he limits to the remembrance of Allah (dhikr): it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: a long dhikr that is called a sermon is necessary. If he gives the sermon sitting, or without purity: it is permissible, but disliked. He prays for the believing men and women, and the loud voice is in the second sermon, not the first. His statement: (and he gives the sermon standing with purity); because the standing in it is inherited (from the Prophet). And it is narrated that Ibn Mas'ud (RA) was asked about that, so he said to the questioner: Do you not recite the saying of Allah: (And they leave you standing) [Jumu'ah:11]. His statement: (if he limits to the remembrance of Allah: it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa); due to His saying: (hasten to the remembrance of Allah) [Jumu'ah:9], and He did not specify. This is when it is with the intention of the sermon. As for if he sneezes and praises Allah, or glorifies, or says la ilaha illa Allah out of wonder at something: that does not substitute for the sermon, by consensus. His statement: (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: a long dhikr that is called a sermon is necessary), and its minimum is from the saying: al-Tahiyyatu lillah... until... His slave and His Messenger; because the sermon is obligatory, and tasbih is not called a sermon. His statement: (and if he gives the sermon sitting, or without purity: it is permissible); because the objective is achieved, which is remembrance and admonition. (But) it is disliked; due to the separation between them and the prayer.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn of Al-Quduri regarding the Friday khutbah. It addresses the requirement of two sermons separated by a sitting, the content of the khutbah, the conditions of standing and purity, and the differences within the Hanafi school and with al-Shafi'i. The author first states the basic ruling: the imam must deliver two sermons with a sitting between them; if the sermon is given after the prayer or before noon, the Friday prayer is invalid. The measure of the two sermons is a surah from the long ones of Mufassal (from Surah Qaf to Surah al-Buruj). The recitation of Quran in the sermon is Sunnah for Hanafis, while al-Shafi'i considers it obligatory. The sitting between the two sermons is not a condition (shart) for Hanafis but merely a rest; al-Shafi'i considers it a condition. Al-Khujandi then outlines the Sunnah content of the sermon: praise of Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, admonition, Quran recitation, standing, and purity. A dispute arises regarding the minimum content: Abu Hanifa holds that any dhikr (remembrance of Allah) suffices, citing the general command 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (Quran 62:9). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require a long dhikr that is conventionally called a khutbah, with a minimum like the Tashahhud. The standing and purity are not obligatory; giving the sermon sitting or without purity is permissible but disliked. The loud voice is recommended in the second sermon, not the first.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered on Friday before the prayer, consisting of two parts separated by a sitting.
قعدة (qa'dah): The sitting between the two Friday sermons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if the Friday khutbah is delivered after the prayer?
A) The prayer is valid but disliked.
B) The prayer is invalid.
C) The prayer is valid if the khutbah was long.
D) The prayer must be repeated with a new khutbah.

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah must be two sermons separated by a sitting, delivered after noon and before prayer; the sitting is not a condition but a rest.

The Content of the Friday Khutbah: Minimum Dhikr and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains rulings of Friday khutbah, its conditions, and internal Hanafi disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the minimum content of the Friday khutbah and apply the ruling to scenarios.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: any dhikr suffices for the khutbah; Sahibayn: a long dhikr conventionally called a khutbah is required.

The passage delves into the requirements for the content of the Friday khutbah, highlighting a significant internal Hanafi ikhtilaf. We will examine the evidence from the Quran and the arguments of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed point
The minimum content that constitutes a valid khutbah according to the Hanafi school.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Any dhikr (remembrance of Allah) suffices. Evidence: Quran 62:9 'فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ' (hasten to the remembrance of Allah) without specification.
This includes saying 'SubhanAllah' or 'Alhamdulillah' with the intention of khutbah.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
A long dhikr that is conventionally called a khutbah is necessary. Minimum: the Tashahhud phrase 'التحيات لله... عبده ورسوله'.
They argue that tasbih (glorification) is not called a khutbah.
4
Analyze the evidence
Abu Hanifa relies on the general command. The Sahibayn rely on the customary meaning of 'khutbah' as a specific form of address.
The passage also states that sneezing with 'Alhamdulillah' does not substitute by consensus.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If someone says only 'SubhanAllah' with intention of khutbah: Abu Hanifa says valid; Sahibayn say invalid.
The mufta bihi is not explicitly given, but later practice tends towards the Sahibayn.

باب صلاة الجمعة - يخطب الإمامُ خُطبتين يَفْصِلُ بينهما بقعدة . ولو خطب بعد الصلاة، أو قبل الزوال: لا تجوز الجمعة. قوله : (يخطب الإمام خطبتين يفصل بينهما بقعدة). ومقدارهما : مقدار سورة من طوال المفصل. ومقدار ما يقرأ فيها من القرآن ثلاث آيات قصار، أو آية طويلة. وقراءة القرآن في الخطبة: سنة عندنا. وقال الشافعي: واجبة. ومقدار الجلوس بينهما عند الطحاوي: مقدار ما يَمَس موضعَ جلوسه من المنبر. وفي ظاهر الرواية : مقدار ثلاث آيات. كذا في «الفتاوى». قال في «النهاية»: وهذه القعدة عندنا للاستراحة، وليست بشرط. وعند الشافعي: شرط. حتى لا يُكتفى عنده بالخطبة الواحدة وإن طالت. - قال الخُجَندي: السُّنَّة في الخُطبة أن يحمد الله، ويُثني عليه، ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ويعظ الناس، ويقرأ القرآن، ويخطب قائماً على طهارة . فإن اقتصر على ذكر الله تعالى : جاز عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا بد من ذِكْرٍ طويل يُسمى خُطبة. وإن خطب قاعداً، أو على غير طهارة : جاز، ويكره . ويدعو للمؤمنين والمؤمنات، ويكون الجهرُ فى الخطبة الثانية دون الأولى. * قوله : (ويخطب قائماً على طهارة)؛ لأن القيام فيها متوارث. وروي أن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه سئل عن ذلك، فقال للسائل: ألست تتلو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَتَرَكُوكَ فَأَيما. الجمعة / ١١ . * قوله: (فإن اقتصر على ذكر الله تعالى: جاز عند أبي حنيفة)؛ لقوله تعالى: (فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ ). الجمعة ٩ ، ولم يفصل. وهذا إذا كان على قصد الخطبة، أما إذا عطس، فحمد الله، أو سبح، أو هلل متعجباً من شيء: فإنه لا ينوب عن الخطبة، إجماعاً. * قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد لا بد من ذكرٍ طويل يسمى خطبة)، وأدناه من قوله : التحيات لله إلى... قوله: عبده ورسوله؛ لأن الخطبة هي الواجبة، والتسبيح: لا يسمى خطبة. قوله: (وإن خطب قاعداً ، أو على غير طهارة: جاز)؛ لحصول المقصود، وهو الذكر والوعظ، (إلا) أنه يكره) ؛ لما فيه من الفصل بينهما وبين الصلاة.
Chapter of Friday Prayer - The Imam delivers two sermons, separating them with a sitting. If he gives the sermon after the prayer, or before noon, the Friday prayer is not valid. His statement: (The Imam delivers two sermons, separating them with a sitting). Their measure: the measure of a surah from the long ones of Mufassal. And the measure of what is recited in it of Quran is three short verses, or one long verse. And recitation of Quran in the sermon: is Sunnah according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: obligatory. The measure of the sitting between them according to al-Tahawi: the measure of what touches his sitting place from the minbar. And in the apparent narration: the measure of three verses. Likewise in al-Fatawa. He said in al-Nihaya: This sitting according to us is for rest, and it is not a condition. According to al-Shafi'i: it is a condition. Such that one sermon is not sufficient for him even if long. Al-Khujandi said: The Sunnah in the sermon is to praise Allah, extol Him, send blessings on the Prophet (SAW), admonish the people, recite Quran, and give the sermon standing with purity. If he limits to the remembrance of Allah (dhikr): it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: a long dhikr that is called a sermon is necessary. If he gives the sermon sitting, or without purity: it is permissible, but disliked. He prays for the believing men and women, and the loud voice is in the second sermon, not the first. His statement: (and he gives the sermon standing with purity); because the standing in it is inherited (from the Prophet). And it is narrated that Ibn Mas'ud (RA) was asked about that, so he said to the questioner: Do you not recite the saying of Allah: (And they leave you standing) [Jumu'ah:11]. His statement: (if he limits to the remembrance of Allah: it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa); due to His saying: (hasten to the remembrance of Allah) [Jumu'ah:9], and He did not specify. This is when it is with the intention of the sermon. As for if he sneezes and praises Allah, or glorifies, or says la ilaha illa Allah out of wonder at something: that does not substitute for the sermon, by consensus. His statement: (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: a long dhikr that is called a sermon is necessary), and its minimum is from the saying: al-Tahiyyatu lillah... until... His slave and His Messenger; because the sermon is obligatory, and tasbih is not called a sermon. His statement: (and if he gives the sermon sitting, or without purity: it is permissible); because the objective is achieved, which is remembrance and admonition. (But) it is disliked; due to the separation between them and the prayer.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn of Al-Quduri regarding the Friday khutbah. It addresses the requirement of two sermons separated by a sitting, the content of the khutbah, the conditions of standing and purity, and the differences within the Hanafi school and with al-Shafi'i. The author first states the basic ruling: the imam must deliver two sermons with a sitting between them; if the sermon is given after the prayer or before noon, the Friday prayer is invalid. The measure of the two sermons is a surah from the long ones of Mufassal (from Surah Qaf to Surah al-Buruj). The recitation of Quran in the sermon is Sunnah for Hanafis, while al-Shafi'i considers it obligatory. The sitting between the two sermons is not a condition (shart) for Hanafis but merely a rest; al-Shafi'i considers it a condition. Al-Khujandi then outlines the Sunnah content of the sermon: praise of Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, admonition, Quran recitation, standing, and purity. A dispute arises regarding the minimum content: Abu Hanifa holds that any dhikr (remembrance of Allah) suffices, citing the general command 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (Quran 62:9). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require a long dhikr that is conventionally called a khutbah, with a minimum like the Tashahhud. The standing and purity are not obligatory; giving the sermon sitting or without purity is permissible but disliked. The loud voice is recommended in the second sermon, not the first.

Key Terms
ذكر طويل (dhikr tawīl): A long remembrance that is conventionally called a khutbah, e.g., the Tashahhud.
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered on Friday before the prayer, consisting of two parts separated by a sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum content of the Friday khutbah according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?
A) Any remembrance of Allah.
B) A long dhikr that is conventionally called a khutbah, minimum like the Tashahhud.
C) Recitation of at least three verses of Quran.
D) Praise of Allah and sending blessings on the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The minimum content of the Friday khutbah is disputed within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa requires any dhikr; the Sahibayn require a long dhikr called a khutbah.

The Shafi'i Disputes: Recitation of Quran and the Sitting as Conditions
Explains rulings of Friday khutbah, its conditions, and internal Hanafi disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main differences between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the Friday khutbah and explain the practical consequences.

Core Idea
For Shafi'is, reciting Quran in khutbah is wajib and the sitting is a condition; Hanafis consider both as sunnah.

This lesson examines the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf on the Friday khutbah. The passage specifically contrasts the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on Quran recitation and the sitting between sermons.

Guided Path
1
State the first disputed point
Recitation of Quran in the khutbah: Hanafis say sunnah; Shafi'is say wajib.
The passage states: 'وقراءة القرآن في الخطبة: سنة عندنا. وقال الشافعي: واجبة'.
2
State the second disputed point
The sitting between the two sermons: Hanafis say not a condition; Shafi'is say it is a condition.
The passage: 'هذه القعدة عندنا للاستراحة، وليست بشرط. وعند الشافعي: شرط'.
3
Identify the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi position is based on the general practice; sitting is not obligatory from the Sunnah.
No specific Quranic or hadith evidence is cited in the passage for this.
4
Identify the Shafi'i dalil (inferred)
Shafi'is likely consider the Prophet's consistent practice as indicating obligation.
The passage does not elaborate the Shafi'i proof.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
If Quran not recited or sitting omitted: Hanafi prayer valid; Shafi'i prayer invalid.
Practical difference: validity of Jumu'ah in these scenarios.

Conditions of Friday Prayer: Congregation and the Khatib's Purity
States conditions and scenarios of Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that congregation is a condition for Friday prayer and apply the rulings when the khatib becomes impure before, during, or after the sermon.

Core Idea
Congregation is a condition for Friday prayer; the khatib's purity is not required for the sermon but affects substitution.

The Friday prayer has unique conditions that distinguish it from daily prayers. One of the most important is the requirement of congregation (jama'ah). Additionally, the state of the khatib (sermon-giver) can raise practical questions: what happens if he loses his wudu after the sermon but before the prayer? Does he need to repeat the sermon? This lesson unpacks these scenarios and highlights a subtle disagreement within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of congregation
The passage begins by reiterating that congregation is a condition (shart) for Friday prayer. Without it, the prayer is invalid. This is unique to Friday; for daily prayers, congregation is a sunnah.
The condition is explicitly stated at the end: 'ومن شرائطها : الجماعة'.
2
Analyze the dispute on purity for the sermon
Abu Yusuf holds that the sermon requires purity like prayer, but the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) disagree. Identify the evidence each side uses: Abu Yusuf draws an analogy to prayer; the majority points to differences (facing away from qibla, speech not invalidating).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is that the sermon is valid without purity, though disliked.
3
Apply the hadath scenarios after the sermon
If the khatib becomes impure after finishing the sermon, he may perform wudu and lead the prayer without repeating the sermon. If he leaves (e.g., eats lunch), he must repeat the sermon.
Key distinction: hadath after sermon does not require repetition; leaving for an unrelated act does.
4
Distinguish hadath before vs. during prayer
If the khatib becomes impure after starting the prayer, he may appoint a substitute even if the substitute did not hear the sermon, because the prayer has already begun. If he becomes impure before starting, the substitute must have heard the sermon.
The rationale: once the prayer is in progress, the sermon's condition is already fulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند أبي يوسف: لا تجوز الخطبة بدون الطهارة؛ لأنها بمنزلة الصلاة، حتى لا تجوز قبل الوقت.
قلنا : ليست كالصلاة؛ لأنها تُؤدى مستدبر القبلة، ولا يُفسدها الكلام.
وكذا لو خطب مضطجعاً : أجزأه؛ لحصول المقصود.
ن
ـ ولو خطب صبي يعقل؟
قال بعضهم : لا يجوز؛ لأن لها شبهاً بالصلاة.
وقال بعضهم : يجوز؛ لأنها ذكر، وليست بصلاة.
ولو أن الخطيب لما فرغ من الخطبة سبقه الحدث، فذهب إلى . وتوضأ، وجاء فصلى بهم: جاز.
ولو تغدى في بيته، وجاء : لم يجز أن يصلي بهم ما لم يُعد الخطبة. ولو سبقه الحدث بعد الشروع في الصلاة، فقدم رجلاً ممن شهد
الخطبة، أو لم يشهدها: جاز.
ولو أن الخطيب سبقه الحدث قبل الشروع في الصلاة، فأمر رجلاً يصلي بهم: إن كان المأمور شهد الخطبة جاز، وإلا فلا، بخلاف الأول. والفرق: أن في الأول قد انعقدت الصلاة، فلا يُحتاج إلى الخطبة في
6
حال بقائها، وهنا : لم تنعقد فصار كالإمام نفسه يصلي بغير خطبة.
قوله: (ومن شرائطها : الجماعة).
And according to Abu Yusuf: the sermon is not valid without purity because it is like prayer, so it is not permissible before the time. We said: it is not like prayer because it is performed facing away from the qibla, and speech does not invalidate it. Likewise, if he delivers the sermon lying down, it suffices because the purpose is achieved. And if an intelligent boy delivers the sermon? Some said it is not permissible because it resembles prayer. Some said it is permissible because it is remembrance and not prayer. If the khatib after finishing the sermon is overtaken by a hadath and goes to perform wudu, then comes and prays with them, it is permissible. If he eats lunch at home and comes, it is not permissible for him to lead them in prayer unless he repeats the sermon. If he is overtaken by a hadath after starting the prayer, and he brings forward a man who witnessed the sermon or did not witness it, it is permissible. If the khatib is overtaken by a hadath before starting the prayer, and he commands a man to lead them in prayer: if the appointed man witnessed the sermon, it is permissible; otherwise not, unlike the first case. The difference is that in the first case the prayer has already begun, so the sermon is not needed during its continuation, and here it has not begun, so it becomes like the imam himself praying without a sermon. His saying: (And among its conditions is congregation).
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage addresses additional conditions for the Friday prayer and various scenarios involving the khatib's state. It begins by noting Abu Yusuf's stricter view that the sermon requires purity like prayer, but the author refutes this by pointing out that the sermon can be performed facing away from the qibla and is not invalidated by speech. The sermon delivered while lying down is also valid. The issue of a boy delivering the sermon is disputed: some analogize to prayer (requiring adulthood), others consider it valid as mere remembrance. The main focus is on the effect of the khatib's hadath (loss of wudu). If the khatib becomes impure after the sermon but before the prayer, he may perform wudu and lead the prayer with the same sermon; if he leaves completely (e.g., for lunch), he must repeat the sermon. If he becomes impure during the prayer, he can appoint a substitute who may or may not have heard the sermon; such substitution is valid because the prayer is already in progress. However, if he becomes impure before the prayer starts, the substitute must have heard the sermon, otherwise the prayer would be without a sermon. Finally, the text reiterates that congregation (jama'ah) is a condition for Friday prayer.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): Congregation; a condition for the validity of Friday prayer.
الحدث (al-hadath): State of ritual impurity (minor or major) that invalidates wudu or ghusl.
شرائط (shurūṭ): Conditions; prerequisites for the validity of an act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a khatib becomes impure (hadath) after finishing the sermon but before starting the prayer, what should he do?
A) The prayer is invalid; he must repeat the sermon and prayer.
B) He may go and perform wudu and then lead the prayer; the same sermon suffices.
C) He must appoint a substitute who witnessed the sermon, else the prayer is invalid.
D) He may lead the prayer without wudu because the sermon is already valid.

Key Takeaway
Congregation is a condition for Friday prayer; the khatib's hadath after the sermon does not require repetition of the sermon, only wudu.

Condition of Purity for the Friday Sermon and Child's Sermon
Dispute on purity for sermon and child's sermon validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on purity for the Friday sermon and explain the reasoning that distinguishes the sermon from prayer.

Core Idea
Purity is not required for the Friday sermon because the sermon is not like prayer—it can be delivered facing away from the qibla and speech does not invalidate it.

The Friday sermon is a central element of Jumu'ah, but does it require wudu? This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira presents an intra-Hanafi debate between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, with implications for the validity of the prayer. It also addresses whether a discerning child can deliver the sermon. Let's explore the arguments and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on purity
Identify the relied-upon ruling: purity is not a condition for the Friday sermon. The sermon is valid without wudu.
This is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Abu Yusuf requires wudu for the sermon, arguing it is like prayer (qiyas). He also claims it cannot be before the time, just like prayer.
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement; the Shafi'i school also requires purity.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The text rebuts: the sermon is not like prayer because it can be given facing away from the qibla and speech does not invalidate it. These are essential differences that break the analogy.
The response uses 'قلنا' (we said) to present the dominant Hanafi view.
4
Extend the principle to other cases
The text then applies the same reasoning: delivering the sermon while lying down is valid because the purpose is achieved. Similarly, a discerning child can deliver the sermon because it is dhikr, not prayer.
These examples reinforce that the sermon is flexible and not bound by prayer's conditions.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the imam delivers the sermon without wudu, according to Abu Hanifa the prayer is valid; according to Abu Yusuf the prayer is invalid (since the sermon is a condition).
The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa, so the prayer is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الجمعة ومن شرائطها : الجماعة، وعند أبي يوسف: لا تجوز الخطبة بدون الطهارة؛ لأنها بمنزلة الصلاة، حتى لا تجوز قبل الوقت. قلنا : ليست كالصلاة؛ لأنها تُؤدى مستدبر القبلة، ولا يُفسدها الكلام. وكذا لو خطب مضطجعاً : أجزأه؛ لحصول المقصود. ولو خطب صبي يعقل؟ قال بعضهم : لا يجوز؛ لأن لها شبهاً بالصلاة. وقال بعضهم : يجوز؛ لأنها ذكر، وليست بصلاة.
Chapter of Friday Prayer. Among its conditions is congregation. According to Abu Yusuf: the sermon is not valid without purity because it is like prayer, such that it is not valid before the time. We said: It is not like prayer because it is performed facing away from the qibla and speech does not invalidate it. Similarly, if he delivered the sermon lying down: it suffices, because the purpose is achieved. And if a discerning child delivers the sermon? Some said: it is not valid because it resembles prayer. Some said: it is valid because it is remembrance, not prayer.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute regarding the condition of purity for the Friday sermon. The matn likely stated the condition of congregation; the commentator then addresses a subsidiary issue about purity according to Abu Yusuf. Abu Yusuf analogizes the sermon to prayer, requiring wudu. Abu Hanifa and others rebut that the sermon is not like prayer since one can face away from the qibla and speech does not nullify it. Hence the sermon is valid without wudu, even if delivered lying down. The final part discusses a child delivering the sermon; the prevailing Hanafi view permits it since it is dhikr, not prayer.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The Friday sermon delivered before the prayer
الطهارة (al-taharah): Ritual purity (wudu or greater)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is obligatory.
B) No, it is not required; the sermon is valid without it.
C) Only if the imam has had a hadath.
D) It is required only for the first khutbah.

Key Takeaway
The Friday sermon in the Hanafi school does not require wudu; it is distinguished from prayer by its permissibility of not facing the qibla and speech during it.

Imam's Hadath After the Sermon: Timing and Substitute Validity
Rulings on imam's hadath after sermon and substitute imam's validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on the imam's hadath after the Friday sermon to determine whether a substitute imam is valid, based on when the hadath occurs.

Core Idea
The validity of a substitute imam depends on whether the prayer had commenced before the imam's hadath.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on what happens when the imam experiences a hadath (event nullifying wudu) after delivering the Friday sermon but before or during the prayer. The key distinction is whether the prayer has already started (after takbir). Understanding this distinction ensures the congregation's prayer remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and key condition
The Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) requires a sermon (khutbah) for its validity. Identify that the sermon is a condition (shart) for the prayer.
2
Consider the first scenario: hadath after sermon but before prayer
If the imam has a hadath after finishing the sermon but before starting the prayer, he may go and perform wudu. If he returns without any intervening act that breaks the continuity (e.g., eating a meal), he can lead the prayer without repeating the sermon. If he eats, the condition of continuity is broken and he must repeat the sermon.
The principle of continuity (muwalat) between sermon and prayer is at play.
3
Consider the second scenario: hadath during prayer
If the hadath occurs after the imam has commenced the prayer (i.e., after takbir), he can appoint a substitute. In this case, the substitute does not need to have attended the sermon, because the condition of the sermon is already fulfilled at the start of the prayer.
4
Consider the third scenario: hadath before prayer, substitute appointed
If the hadath occurs before the prayer begins, the imam can appoint a substitute only if that substitute attended the sermon. Otherwise, the prayer would be like an imam praying without a sermon, which invalidates it.
5
Understand the legal reasoning
The distinction hinges on whether the prayer has been 'commenced' (in'aqad). Once the prayer has started, its conditions are locked in; the sermon is no longer needed. If not commenced, the substitute must fulfill all conditions, including having heard the sermon.
This is a qiyas: the case of a substitute before commencement is like the imam himself praying without a sermon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أن الخطيب لما فرغ من الخطبة سبقه الحدث، فذهب إلى . وتوضأ، وجاء فصلى بهم: جاز. ولو تغدى في بيته، وجاء : لم يجز أن يصلي بهم ما لم يُعد الخطبة. ولو سبقه الحدث بعد الشروع في الصلاة، فقدم رجلاً ممن شهد الخطبة، أو لم يشهدها: جاز. ولو أن الخطيب سبقه الحدث قبل الشروع في الصلاة، فأمر رجلاً يصلي بهم: إن كان المأمور شهد الخطبة جاز، وإلا فلا، بخلاف الأول. والفرق: أن في الأول قد انعقدت الصلاة، فلا يُحتاج إلى الخطبة في حال بقائها، وهنا : لم تنعقد فصار كالإمام نفسه يصلي بغير خطبة.
And if the khatib, after finishing the sermon, was overtaken by a hadath, so he went and performed wudu, and came and led them in prayer: it is permissible. And if he had lunch in his house and came: it is not permissible for him to lead them unless he repeats the sermon. And if he was overtaken by a hadath after beginning the prayer, and he appointed a man who had attended the sermon, or even if he had not attended it: it is permissible. And if the khatib was overtaken by a hadath before beginning the prayer, and he ordered a man to lead them: if the appointed man had attended the sermon it is permissible, otherwise not, contrary to the first case. The difference is that in the first case the prayer has already commenced, so the sermon is not needed during its continuation, whereas here it has not commenced, so it becomes like the imam himself praying without a sermon.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage details rulings when the imam has a hadath after finishing the sermon but before or during the prayer. The key principle: if the hadath occurs after the prayer has started (after takbir), the imam can appoint any substitute (even one who did not hear the sermon) because the sermon's condition is already fulfilled. If the hadath occurs before the prayer starts, the substitute must have heard the sermon, otherwise the prayer is not valid (since the sermon condition would be missing). Also, if the imam leaves to eat after the sermon, he must repeat the sermon because the state of being a valid imam is broken.

Key Terms
الحدث (al-hadath): An event that nullifies wudu (e.g., passing wind)
الشروع في الصلاة (al-shurū‘ fī al-ṣalāh): The commencement of the prayer, i.e., after saying the opening takbir
الخطبة (al-khuṭbah): The sermon delivered before Friday prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam has a hadath after the takbir (i.e., during prayer), can he appoint a substitute who did not attend the sermon?
A) Yes, it is permissible.
B) No, it is not permissible.
C) Only if the substitute is also a khatib.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The timing of the imam's hadath—before or after prayer commencement—determines whether the substitute must have attended the sermon.

The Congregation Condition in Friday Prayer: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explanation of congregation condition and ikhtilaf among Hanafi imams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the congregation condition for Friday prayer and apply them to determine the validity of the prayer when the congregation disperses.

Core Idea
The timing of the congregation condition determines whether Friday prayer reverts to Zuhr.

Friday prayer requires congregation, but what exactly does this mean? The Hanafi school has a nuanced internal debate about the precise nature of this condition. This lesson unpacks the views of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar, and shows you how their differences play out in a real scenario. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply conditions in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the contested condition
The act is Friday prayer. What is the condition in dispute? The passage states: 'congregation is a condition.' But what kind of condition? Three Hanafi imams disagree.
2
State the three positions
Abu Hanifa: condition for emphasized validity (shart al-in'iqaad al-mu'akkad) by one rak'ah. Sahibayn: condition for initial validity (shart al-in'iqaad al-mubtada'). Zufar: condition for continuance (shart al-dawaam).
3
Apply each position to the scenario of dispersal
Case 1: Dispersal after starting but before tying to prostration (sajdah). According to Sahibayn, it remains Friday; according to Abu Hanifa, it becomes Zuhr. Case 2: Dispersal after prostration. All except Zufar agree it remains Friday (Zufar says invalid).
4
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is whether the prayer is completed as Friday or must be switched to Zuhr. This affects the imam's decision when the congregation leaves early.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: congregation is a condition for initial validity. Abu Hanifa's view is known but not operative in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومن شرائطها : الجماعة). وهي شرط الانعقاد المبتدأ عندهما. وعند أبي حنيفة : شرط الانعقاد المؤكد، وذلك بالركعة. وعند زفر : شرط الدوام. وفائدته فيما إذا نفروا عنه بعد الشروع قبل التقييد بالسجدة: فعندهما يتمُّها جمعة، وعند أبي حنيفة: يستقبل الظهر. ولو نفروا بعد السجود : أتمها جمعةً، خلافاً لزفر.
His saying: (Among its conditions is congregation). And it is a condition for the initial validity according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Abu Hanifa: it is a condition for emphasized validity, and that is by one rak'ah. According to Zufar: it is a condition for continuance. Its benefit is in the case when they leave after starting but before tying to the prostration: according to the two they complete it as Friday, according to Abu Hanifa they pray Zuhr. And if they leave after prostration: they complete it as Friday, contrary to Zufar.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage discusses the precise legal nature of the congregation requirement for Friday prayer. The matn lists congregation as a condition. The commentator explains that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, congregation is a condition for the validity of starting the prayer (shart al-in'iqaad al-mubtada'). According to Abu Hanifa, it is a condition for the validity that is emphasized (shart al-in'iqaad al-mu'akkad), meaning that if the congregation leaves after one rak'ah, the prayer becomes Zuhr. According to Zufar, it is a condition for the continuance (shart al-dawaam), meaning if the congregation leaves at any point, the prayer becomes invalid. The practical difference is shown: if people leave before tying to prostration (i.e., before sajda), the prayer is saved as Friday for the two, but becomes Zuhr for Abu Hanifa; after sajda, all except Zufar consider it Friday.

Key Terms
شرط الانعقاد (shart al-in'iqaad): Condition for the validity of the act from its inception
شرط الانعقاد المبتدأ (shart al-in'iqaad al-mubtada'): Condition for the initial validity of the act (according to the Sahibayn)
شرط الانعقاد المؤكد (shart al-in'iqaad al-mu'akkad): Condition for emphasized validity (according to Abu Hanifa)
شرط الدوام (shart al-dawaam): Condition for continuance (according to Zufar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which scenario would Zufar consider invalid for Friday prayer?
A) Congregation leaves after starting but before tying to prostration.
B) Congregation leaves after prostration.
C) Congregation leaves before the start of the prayer.
D) Congregation stays for the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
The nature of the congregation condition for Friday prayer is nuanced within the Hanafi school; the relied-upon view (Sahibayn) treats it as a condition for initial validity, which means once the prayer starts with a congregation, it continues as Friday unless the congregation fails to complete the first rak'ah.

Late Takbir in Jumu'ah: The Intra-Hanafi Time Limit
Dispute on when latecomers' failure to takbir invalidates Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the latest time the congregation can say the opening takbir in Friday prayer and apply the correct ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is invalid if the congregation delays takbir beyond a certain point; three imams disagree on where that point is.

This lesson examines a fiqh scenario where the entire congregation fails to say the opening takbir until after the imam has already begun the prayer. The Hanafi school has three different rulings on how much delay is too much. Understanding these positions is crucial for correctly judging the validity of Friday prayers in real-life congregations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
Read the first part of the passage: if the congregation delays the takbir until after the imam finishes thana' and starts reciting a short verse, the prayer is invalid for all.
This is the strictest view.
2
Understand the dispute timeline
Note that Abu Yusuf allows a longer delay: the takbir is still valid if made before the imam recites three short verses or one long verse. Muhammad allows even longer: before the imam raises his head from ruku.
These are progressively more lenient.
3
Compare the three thresholds
Line up the events: thana' completion → recitation of one short verse → recitation of three short verses → ruku' → raising head. Each imam sets a different cutoff along this timeline.
4
Determine the practical consequence
For each view, state whether the prayer is valid or invalid. The initial ruling says invalid after thana'+short verse; Abu Yusuf says valid until after three short verses; Muhammad says valid until after ruku' (before raising head).
The most lenient view saves many prayers.
5
Note the absence of tarjih
The passage does not give a preferred view. In later fatwa practice, Muhammad's view is often relied upon for ease, but the mufti may choose based on circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كبر الإمام، وتغافل القوم ، ولم يكبروا حتى فرغ من الثناء، وأخذ في القراءة مقدار آية قصيرة، ثم كبروا : فسدت الجمعة للإمام والقوم جميعاً. أما لو كبروا قبل أن يأخذ في القراءة: تجوز الجمعة. وقال أبو يوسف: إن كبروا قبل أن يقرأ ثلاث آيات قصار، أو آية طويلة : صحت الجمعة، وإلا فلا. وقال محمد: إن شرعوا قبل أن يرفع رأسه من الركوع: صحت الجمعة، وإلا فلا.
And if the imam said the takbir, and the people were heedless and did not say the takbir until he finished the thana' and began reciting the amount of a short verse, then they said the takbir: the Friday prayer is invalid for both the imam and the people. But if they said the takbir before he began reciting: the Friday prayer is valid. Abu Yusuf said: if they said the takbir before he recited three short verses or one long verse: the Friday prayer is valid, otherwise not. Muhammad said: if they began before he raised his head from bowing: the Friday prayer is valid, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where the congregation delays their opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) after the imam has started. According to the initial statement, if they delay until the imam finishes the thana' (subhanaka) and begins reciting even a short verse, the prayer is invalid for everyone. However, if they join before he starts reciting, it is valid. Then Abu Yusuf and Muhammad offer more lenient views: Abu Yusuf allows until after three short verses or one long verse; Muhammad allows until before the imam raises his head from ruku. The difference hinges on when the latecomers are considered to have missed the congregation for Friday prayer. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Yusuf or Muhammad? The text does not give a tarjih, but the initial statement seems stricter.

Key Terms
الثناء (al-thana'): The opening supplication (subhanaka allahumma...) recited after takbir

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If they delay until after the imam finishes the thana' and starts reciting.
B) If they delay until after the imam bows.
C) If they delay until after the first prostration.
D) If they delay until after the imam says the taslim.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has three views on the latest permissible time for the congregation to make the opening takbir in Friday prayer; the strictest is after thana', the most lenient is before the imam raises from ruku.

Who Can Be Led in Friday Prayer When People Leave
Rulings on leading Friday prayer when only women/children or slaves/travelers remain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leading Friday prayer when only women, children, slaves, travelers, or sick remain, and identify the eligibility condition for the imam.

Core Idea
Only free adult male residents can be imams; women and children cannot be led, but slaves, travelers, and sick can.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayira addresses a practical scenario: after the Friday sermon, some people leave, leaving only certain categories. The imam must decide whether to proceed. The ruling hinges on the eligibility of the remaining congregation to serve as imams themselves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage describes two outcomes after the sermon: either only women/children remain, or only slaves/travelers/sick remain. Note the difference.
Women and children are not 'ahl al-jumu'ah'.
2
State the ruling for each
If only women/children remain, the imam does not lead Friday prayer. If slaves/travelers/sick remain, he does lead.
The ruling is clear and unconditional.
3
Explain the reason
Women and children are not eligible to be imams for Friday prayer because it is not obligatory on them. Imamate requires eligibility to be an imam oneself.
Eligibility means being a free, adult, resident male.
4
Identify 'ahl al-jumu'ah'
Ahl al-jumu'ah are those obligated to attend: free, adult, resident males. Only they can be imams.
Slaves, travelers, and sick are not obligated but are eligible.
5
Apply the rule
Practice with hypotheticals: if only women remain, do not lead; if a mix of women and one traveler, you may lead because the traveler is eligible.
The presence of at least one eligible person suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو خطب، ونَفَرَ عنه الناس، ولم يبق معه إلا النساء أو الصبيان: لم يصل بهم الجمعة؛ لأنهم ليسوا من أهلها أي لا يجوز أن يكونوا أئمةً. وإن بقي معه عبيد، أو مسافرون، أو مرضى : صلى بهم الجمعة.
And if he delivered the sermon, and the people dispersed, and only women or children remained with him: he should not lead them in Friday prayer because they are not among its people, i.e., they are not eligible to be imams. And if slaves, travelers, or sick people remained with him: he leads them in Friday prayer.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage gives a clear rule: the imam can only lead Friday prayer if the remaining congregation consists of individuals who are eligible to be imams (i.e., free, adult, resident males). Women and children are not eligible to be imams for Friday prayer because Friday prayer is not obligatory upon them and they cannot represent the congregation. However, slaves (who are not required to pray Friday but can participate), travelers (who are not residents), and sick people (who may have excuse) are eligible to be led in Friday prayer, so the imam can proceed.

Key Terms
أهل الجمعة (ahl al-jumu'ah): Those obliged to attend Friday prayer: free, adult, resident males

Key Takeaway
The imam of Friday prayer must have at least one eligible person (free, adult, resident male) in the congregation; women and children do not fulfill this condition.

The Congregation's Joining Condition in Friday Prayer: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the condition for congregation joining and rulings on departure and delayed takbir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the congregation's joining condition (shart al-in'iqad) in Friday prayer and apply the practical difference when the congregation departs before prostration.

Core Idea
The congregation's joining condition for Friday prayer is disputed among Hanafi imams—initial, confirmed by rak'ah, or continuous.

Friday prayer requires the congregation to join the imam. But what exactly is the condition for that joining? The Hanafi school contains multiple views. In this lesson, we explore the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and Zufar, and see how these differences affect the validity of Friday prayer when the congregation departs or delays their takbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Name the three shurut: mubtada' (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) – initial joining; mu'akkad (Abu Hanifa) – confirmed joining by at least one rak'ah; dawam (Zufar) – continuity throughout the prayer.
Note that 'shart al-in'iqad' refers to the condition for the validity of Friday prayer.
2
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence of the dispute appears when the congregation departs after starting but before prostration. According to Sahibayn, they complete as Friday; according to Abu Hanifa, they switch to Dhuhr; according to Zufar, if they depart at any time, the prayer becomes invalid.
Focus on the case of departure before prostration.
3
Analyze the delayed takbir rulings
Examine the scenario where the congregation delays their takbir after the imam's takbir. The text gives thresholds from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Understand the variations and how they affect validity.
These rulings are additional details derived from the main condition dispute.
4
Evaluate the ruling on remaining congregation
Consider the case where most of the congregation leaves, leaving only women, children, slaves, travelers, or sick persons. Determine in which cases Friday prayer remains valid.
This involves the qualification of the remaining individuals to be imams or to constitute a valid congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الجمعة
وهي شرط الانعقاد المبتدأ عندهما.
وعند أبي حنيفة : شرط الانعقاد المؤكد، وذلك بالركعة.
وعند زفر : شرط الدوام.
وفائدته فيما إذا نفروا عنه بعد الشروع قبل التقييد بالسجدة: فعندهما يتمُّها جمعة، وعند أبي حنيفة: يستقبل الظهر.
ولو نفروا بعد السجود : أتمها جمعةً، خلافاً لزفر.
ولو كبر الإمام، وتغافل القوم ، ولم يكبروا حتى فرغ من الثناء، وأخذ في القراءة مقدار آية قصيرة، ثم كبروا : فسدت الجمعة للإمام والقوم جميعاً.
أما لو كبروا قبل أن يأخذ في القراءة: تجوز الجمعة.
وقال أبو يوسف: إن كبروا قبل أن يقرأ ثلاث آيات قصار، أو آية طويلة : صحت الجمعة، وإلا فلا.
وقال محمد: إن شرعوا قبل أن يرفع رأسه من الركوع: صحت الجمعة، وإلا فلا.
ولو خطب، ونَفَرَ عنه الناس، ولم يبق معه إلا النساء أو الصبيان: لم يُصلِ بهم الجمعة؛ لأنهم ليسوا من أهلها أي لا يجوز أن يكونوا أئمةً.
وإن بقي معه عبيد، أو مسافرون، أو مرضى : صلى بهم الجمعة.
Chapter of Friday Prayer. It (the congregation) is the initial condition of validity according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Abu Hanifa: the confirmed condition of validity, and that is by (joining in) the rak'ah. According to Zufar: the condition of continuity. Its benefit is when they depart from him after starting before (tying) by the prostration: according to them, he completes it as Friday prayer, and according to Abu Hanifa, he performs instead Dhuhr. If they depart after prostration: he completes it as Friday prayer, contrary to Zufar. If the Imam says the takbir, and the people are heedless and do not say takbir until he finishes the thana' and begins reciting the length of a short verse, then they say takbir: the Friday prayer is invalid for both the imam and the people all together. But if they say takbir before he begins reciting: the Friday prayer is valid. Abu Yusuf said: If they say takbir before he recites three short verses or one long verse: the Friday prayer is valid, otherwise not. Muhammad said: If they begin (the takbir) before he raises his head from bowing: the Friday prayer is valid, otherwise not. If he gives the khutbah, and the people depart from him, and only women or boys remain with him: he does not pray Friday prayer with them because they are not from its people, i.e., they are not qualified to be imams. And if slaves, travelers, or sick persons remain with him: he prays Friday prayer with them.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute covering the condition for the congregation joining the imam in Friday prayer and related rulings. The text first defines the condition for the congregation’s joining: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the condition is the initial joining (mubtada'), meaning that the congregation's presence at the start of the prayer is sufficient. According to Abu Hanifa, the condition is a confirmed joining (mu'akkad), which occurs only once the congregation joins in the rak'ah (i.e., at least one rak'ah with the imam). Zufar holds the condition of continuity (da'am), meaning the congregation must remain throughout. The practical difference (thamarah) appears when the congregation departs after starting but before tying the prayer with prostration (sajdah): according to the Sahibayn, they complete it as Friday prayer; according to Abu Hanifa, they must restart and pray Dhuhr. If they depart after prostration, according to Abu Hanifa it is valid as Friday prayer, contrary to Zufar. The passage then discusses a case where the congregation delays their takbir after the imam's takbir. If they do not say takbir until after the imam finishes the thana' (opening supplication) and begins reciting a short verse, the Friday prayer is invalid for all. If they say takbir before the imam begins reciting, the prayer is valid. Abu Yusuf gives a more lenient view: if they say takbir before the imam has recited three short verses or one long verse, the prayer is valid; otherwise not. Muhammad requires them to begin the takbir before the imam raises his head from bowing (i.e., before the imam ends the recitation and goes into ruku'). Finally, the passage addresses a situation where the imam gives the khutbah and the entire congregation departs, leaving only women or children. In that case, Friday prayer is not valid because women and boys are not qualified to be imams. However, if slaves, travelers, or sick persons remain, the prayer is valid as they are eligible for imamah.

Key Terms
شرط الانعقاد المبتدأ (shart al-in‘iqad al-mubtada’): The condition that the congregation joins the imam at the very beginning of the prayer (the opening takbir) for the Friday prayer to be valid.
شرط الانعقاد المؤكد (shart al-in‘iqad al-mu’akkad): The condition that the congregation joins the imam in at least one rak'ah (confirmed joining) for the Friday prayer to be valid.
شرط الدوام (shart al-dawam): The condition that the congregation remains with the imam throughout the entire prayer for the Friday prayer to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens if the congregation departs from the imam after starting the prayer but before prostration (sajdah)?
A) They must complete it as Friday prayer.
B) They must start over and pray Dhuhr.
C) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated as Friday prayer.
D) They may choose to continue as Friday prayer or pray Dhuhr.

Key Takeaway
The condition for the congregation's joining in Friday prayer is a matter of ikhtilaf among Hanafi imams, with practical consequences for the validity of the prayer when departure occurs.

Minimum Number for Friday Prayer and Recitation Rules
Debates minimum congregation for Friday prayer and recitation rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number required for Friday prayer according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, explain the proof for each, and apply the rulings on recitation and congregation change.

Core Idea
Friday prayer requires a congregation; Hanafis dispute whether three or two besides the Imam suffice.

This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the minimum number for Friday prayer and the rules of recitation. We will follow the commentary in Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira to understand the proofs and the practical consequences. Additionally, we address the ruling on recitation aloud and the permissibility of leading a new congregation after the khutbah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The minimum number of participants for Friday prayer besides the Imam is a condition (shart) for its validity.
2
State the positions
Abu Hanifa: three besides Imam; Abu Yusuf: two besides Imam; Muhammad sometimes agrees with Abu Hanifa.
The text states: 'وأقلهم عند أبي حنيفة : ثلاثة سوى الإمام، وقالا : اثنان سوى الإمام'
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
A pair is considered a congregation because the Imam stands ahead of them, as in normal congregational prayer.
The commentary says: 'لأن للمثنى : حكم الجماعة، حتى إن الإمام يتقدم عليهما'
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
The Quranic verse (al-Jumuah 9) uses the plural imperative 'fascaw' (hasten). In Arabic, the minimum plural is three.
The verse: {إِذَا نُودِى لِلصَّلَوةِ مِن يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكر الله}
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If only two besides Imam are present, Abu Hanifa says Friday is invalid and Dhuhr must be prayed; Abu Yusuf says Friday is valid. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
6
Examine recitation rules
The Imam recites aloud in both rak'ahs of Friday prayer, and no specific surah is required; any part of the Quran suffices.
Text: 'ويجهر الإمام بالقراءة في الركعتين . وليس فيهما قراءة سورة بعينها'
7
Examine congregation change
If after the khutbah all attendees leave and new people come, the Imam may lead them in Friday prayer and it is valid, even if they did not hear the khutbah.
Text: 'ولو فرغ من الخطبة، فذهبوا كلهم، وجاء آخرون لم يشهدوا الخطبة، فصلى بهم الجمعة: أجزأه'

Source Text

باب صلاة الجمعة
وأقلهم عند أبي حنيفة : ثلاثة سوى الإمام، وقالا : اثنان سوى الإمام .
ويجهر الإمام بالقراءة في الركعتين .
وليس فيهما قراءة سورة بعينها .
ولو فرغ من الخطبة، فذهبوا كلهم، وجاء آخرون لم يشهدوا الخطبة، فصلى بهم الجمعة: أجزأه.
*
قوله : (وأقلهم عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد (۱): ثلاثة سوى الإمام).
والشرط فيهم : أن يكونوا صالحين للإمامة، أما إذا كانوا لا يصلحون لها، كالنساء والصبيان: لا تصح الجمعة.
* قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف : اثنان سوى الإمام)؛ لأن للمثْنى : حكم الجماعة، حتى إن الإمام يتقدم عليهما.
ولهما: قوله تعالى: ﴿إِذَا نُودِى لِلصَّلَوةِ مِن يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكر الله﴾ الجمعة /۹ ، فهذا يقتضي منادياً، وهو المؤذن، وذاكراً وهو الإمام، وقوله : فاسعوا : خطاب جمع، وأقل الجمع : ثلاثة.

* قوله: (وليس فيهما قراءة سورة بعينها).
Chapter of Friday Prayer. And the minimum of them according to Abu Hanifa: three besides the Imam, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: two besides the Imam. And the Imam recites aloud in the two rak'ahs. And there is no specific surah to be recited in them. And if he finishes the khutbah, and all of them go away, and others come who did not attend the khutbah, and he prays Friday prayer with them: it suffices him. * His saying: (And the minimum of them according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (1): three besides the Imam). And the condition regarding them is that they be qualified for imamah; but if they are not qualified for it, like women and boys, the Friday prayer is not valid. * His saying: (And Abu Yusuf said: two besides the Imam) because the pair has the ruling of a congregation, so much so that the Imam stands ahead of them. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is the saying of the Most High: 'When the call is made for prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (al-Jumuah 9). This necessitates a caller, who is the mu'adhdhin, and a mindful one, who is the Imam, and His saying 'hasten' is an address to a group, and the minimum of a group is three. * His saying: (And the Imam recites aloud in the two rak'ahs) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited aloud in them (2). * His saying: (And there is no specific surah to be recited in them).
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage addresses the minimum number of participants required for Friday prayer and the rules of recitation. The matn (base text) states that according to Abu Hanifa, the minimum is three men besides the Imam, while according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), it is two besides the Imam. The commentary clarifies that Muhammad is included with Abu Hanifa in some versions, though in others he agrees with Abu Yusuf. A crucial condition is that the participants must be qualified for imamah (i.e., free adult Muslim men); women and boys are not sufficient. The proof for the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the Quranic verse (al-Jumuah 9): 'When the call is made for prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah.' The verse implies a caller (mu'adhdhin) and a mindful one (the Imam), and the address 'hasten' is to a group (jam'), and the minimum of a group is three. Abu Yusuf argues that a pair counts as a congregation because the Imam stands ahead of even two followers. The passage then states that the Imam recites aloud in the two rak'ahs of Friday prayer, following the practice of the Prophet, and that there is no requirement to recite a specific surah; any part of the Quran suffices. Finally, a separate ruling: if after the khutbah the entire original congregation leaves and new people arrive who did not hear the khutbah, the Imam may lead them in Friday prayer and it is valid.

Key Terms
سوى الإمام (siwa al-imam): Excluding the Imam; the number of followers required besides the Imam himself.
أقل الجمع (aqall al-jam'): The minimum number that constitutes a group (jam') in Arabic language, which is three according to the Hanafi position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They pray Friday validly.
B) They pray Dhuhr instead.
C) They pray alone.
D) They join with the imam without a congregation.

Key Takeaway
The minimum number for Friday prayer in the Hanafi school is three men besides the Imam (Abu Hanifa's view), based on the Quranic verse requiring a plural group.

Minimum Number for Friday Prayer: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on minimum participants for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the minimum participants for Jumu'ah and identify the Quranic evidence used by each view.

Core Idea
The minimum for Jumu'ah is either three or two men besides the imam—a dispute rooted in Arabic linguistics of jam'.

The Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) is a distinct obligation with its own conditions. One of its conditions is a minimum number of participants. In this lesson, we examine the intra-Hanafi disagreement on that minimum: Abu Hanifa requiring three men besides the imam, and Abu Yusuf (and in some transmissions, Muhammad) requiring two. We will explore the linguistic and legal reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify what each imam holds regarding the minimum number of participants besides the imam.
Abu Hanifa: three; Abu Yusuf: two; Muhammad's view is transmitted both ways.
2
Identify the Quranic proof for Abu Hanifa's view
Locate the verse cited (Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9) and the operative phrase 'fas'aw'.
3
Analyze the linguistic argument
Explain why 'fas'aw' (plural imperative) implies at least three participants.
In Arabic, the minimum plural is three.
4
Examine Abu Yusuf's alternative proof
Understand the argument that the dual (two persons) constitutes a congregation, based on the practice of the imam leading two.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
Apply the difference to a real scenario: if only two men attend besides the imam, which view validates Jumu'ah?
Mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa: Jumu'ah invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الجمعة
وأقلهم عند أبي حنيفة : ثلاثة سوى الإمام، وقالا : اثنان سوى الإمام .
*
قوله : (وأقلهم عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد (۱): ثلاثة سوى الإمام).
والشرط فيهم : أن يكونوا صالحين، للإمامة، أما إذا كانوا لا يصلحون لها، كالنساء والصبيان: لا تصح الجمعة.
* قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف : اثنان سوى الإمام)؛ لأن للمثْنى : حكم الجماعة، حتى إن الإمام يتقدم عليهما.
ولهما: قوله تعالى: ﴿إِذَا نُودِى لِلصَّلَوةِ مِن يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكر الله ﴾ الجمعة /۹، فهذا يقتضي منادياً، وهو المؤذن، وذاكراً وهو الإمام،
وقوله : فاسعوا : خطاب جمع، وأقل الجمع : ثلاثة.
Chapter of Friday Prayer. And the minimum of them according to Abu Hanifa is three besides the imam, and both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: two besides the imam. * He said: (The minimum according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (1): three besides the imam). And the condition in them is that they be fit for imamah; as for if they are not fit for it, such as women and minors, Jumu'ah is not valid. * He said: (Abu Yusuf said: two besides the imam) because the dual has the ruling of a congregation, such that the imam steps ahead of them. And for them (the two): the saying of the Exalted: 'When the call is made for prayer on the day of Jumu'ah, hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (al-Jumu'ah 9). This necessitates a caller, who is the mu'adhdhin, and a rememberer, who is the imam, and His saying 'hasten' is an address to a group, and the minimum of a group is three.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the minimum number of participants required for the validity of Friday prayer (Jumu'ah). The base text (matn) states that according to Abu Hanifa, the minimum is three men in addition to the imam, while according to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), it is two besides the imam. The commentary clarifies that these participants must be eligible for imamah, i.e., free adult males; women and minors do not count. The evidence for the Sahibayn's position is that the dual (two persons) carries the legal status of a congregation (jama'ah), as the imam leads them standing ahead. For their view, they cite the Quranic verse (62:9) which commands 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' using the plural imperative 'fas'aw', which implies at least three (the minimum of a jam' is three). Note: In some manuscripts, Muhammad is aligned with Abu Hanifa, and in others with Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
صلاة الجمعة (salat al-jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer that replaces the Zuhr prayer on Fridays.
إمام (imam): The leader of the congregational prayer.
جمع (jam'): A group; in this context, the minimum number for a plural address is three.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Three
C) Four
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on the minimum Jumu'ah participants: three or two besides the imam, with the relied-upon view being three.

Audible Recitation in Jumu'ah Prayer
Ruling that the Imam recites aloud in Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the imam recites aloud in Jumu'ah and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The imam must recite aloud in Jumu'ah because the Prophet ﷺ did so.

This lesson clarifies a key distinction between the Friday (Jumu'ah) prayer and the noon (Zuhr) prayer: Jumu'ah is a loud prayer, while Zuhr is silent. We examine the explicit ruling and its evidence from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that the imam recites aloud (jahr) in the two rak'ahs of Jumu'ah. Determine the legal category: is this wajib, sunnah, or something else?
In Hanafi fiqh, jahr in Jumu'ah is wajib, not fard, because the proof is a hadith ahad.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the Prophet's action: 'the Prophet ﷺ recited aloud in them.' Identify the source and its authority level.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim, classed as ahad in transmission, but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this proof establish the ruling? The verb 'jahara' (recited aloud) shows a deliberate practice, which becomes the Sunnah for the community.
Hanafi usul: the action of the Prophet (fi'l) indicates obligation when accompanied by a command context, but here it indicates a confirmed practice (sunnah/wajib).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجهر الإمام بالقراءة في الركعتين .
*
قوله: (ويجهر الإمام بالقراءة في الركعتين)؛ لأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام جَهَرَ فيهما (٢).
And the imam recites aloud in the two rak'ahs. * He said: (The imam recites aloud in the two rak'ahs) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited aloud in them (2).
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This is a clear ruling (hukm) that the imam must recite the Quran aloud (jahr) during both rak'ahs of the Friday prayer. The proof (dalil) is the Sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him), as reported in Sahih Muslim (hadith 877). This is consistent with the consensus that Jumu'ah is a loud prayer, unlike Zuhr which is silent. The Hadith reference indicates the basis is the actual practice of the Prophet.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Reciting the Quran audibly in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The imam must recite aloud in Jumu'ah because the Prophet's practice establishes it as a wajib act.

No Specified Surah for Jumu'ah: The Hanafi View
Hanafi vs Shafi'i on specified surahs for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on reciting specific surahs in Jumu'ah prayer and explain the practical difference from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school does not prescribe a specific surah for Jumu'ah; any Quranic passage suffices.

This brief passage from the Quduri matn lays out a clean difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. While both agree that reciting a surah after al-Fatihah is required, they differ on whether particular surahs are recommended. The Hanafi position is that no surah is specified, leaving the imam free to choose any part of the Quran. The Shafi'i school, based on certain hadith, holds it mustahabb to recite Surah al-Jumu'ah in the first rak'ah and Surah al-Munafiqun in the second. Understanding this difference helps avoid confusion about what is obligatory versus recommended in Friday prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act in question
The act under dispute is the recitation of a specific surah (after al-Fatihah) in the two rak'ahs of Jumu'ah prayer.
The basic requirement is to recite some Quranic verses; the dispute is over which surah is recommended.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to the Hanafi school, no specific surah is prescribed. The matn says: 'There is no recitation of a specific surah in them.'
This means the imam may recite any surah or verses he wishes.
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i recommendation
The Shafi'i school recommends reciting Surah al-Jumu'ah in the first rak'ah and Surah al-Munafiqun in the second.
This is based on hadith reports of the Prophet's practice.
4
Recognise the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In practice, a Hanafi imam may choose any surah, while a Shafi'i imam will preferably recite the two specified surahs. Both prayers are valid.
The difference is purely in the level of recommendation, not in obligation.
5
Note the legal category
This is a dispute over mustahabb (recommended) vs. mubah (permissible). Neither school considers it fard or wajib to recite a specific surah.
Thus the prayer remains valid regardless of which surah is recited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس فيهما قراءة سورة بعينها.
وقال الشافعي : يستحب أن يقرأ في الأولى سورة الجمعة، وفي الثانية سورة المنافقين.
And there is no recitation of a specific surah in them. And al-Shafi'i said: It is recommended to recite in the first (rak'ah) Surah al-Jumu'ah, and in the second Surah al-Munafiqun.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage highlights a difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the recited surahs in Friday prayer. The Hanafi position is that no specific surah is prescribed; any portion of the Quran may be recited, as the basic requirement is the recitation of al-Fatihah and some additional verses. The Shafi'i school, based on certain hadith, holds it mustahabb (recommended) to recite Surah al-Jumu'ah in the first rak'ah and Surah al-Munafiqun in the second. This difference is purely one of preference (mandub vs. mustahabb), not obligation. Both schools agree that other surahs are permissible.

Key Terms
سورة الجمعة (Surah al-Jumu'ah): The 62nd chapter of the Quran, named after the Friday prayer.
سورة المنافقين (Surah al-Munafiqun): The 63rd chapter of the Quran, dealing with hypocrites.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is wajib to recite Surah al-Jumu'ah.
B) It is recommended to recite Surah al-Jumu'ah and al-Munafiqun.
C) No specific surah is prescribed.
D) It is mandatory to recite Surah al-Fatihah only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require or recommend any specific surah for Jumu'ah; the imam may choose any surah.

Jumu'ah with New Congregation After Khutbah
Ruling on Jumu'ah validity when new congregation arrives after khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of Jumu'ah when a new congregation arrives after the khutbah and explain why the khutbah is a condition fulfilled by the imam, not an individual obligation.

Core Idea
The khutbah is a condition for Jumu'ah, not an individual obligation; it suffices even if heard only by the imam.

You might assume that every Jumu'ah attendee must hear the khutbah for the prayer to be valid. However, the Hanafi school considers the khutbah a condition of the prayer, not an obligation on each individual. This ruling clarifies that once the imam delivers it correctly and at the proper time, the prayer is valid even for latecomers who missed the sermon entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The text presents a case: after the imam finishes the two-part khutbah, the entire original congregation leaves, and a new group arrives who did not attend the khutbah.
Note the extreme case: everyone leaves, not just a few.
2
State the ruling
The imam leads the new group in the two rak'ahs of Jumu'ah, and the prayer suffices (أجزأه) for both the imam and the new congregation.
The word أجزأه indicates legal sufficiency and validity.
3
Distinguish condition from individual obligation
The khutbah is a condition (shart) for Jumu'ah as a whole, not a requirement on each attendee. Once it is performed at its proper time before the prayer, the condition is met.
This is a distinct Hanafi view; other schools may differ.
4
Identify the key nuance
The ruling applies only if the khutbah was validly delivered at the correct time (before the prayer) and the prayer is still within the Jumu'ah time window.
If the khutbah was invalid or missed, the condition fails.
5
Derive the practical takeaway
The imam does not need to repeat the khutbah for the new congregation. The Jumu'ah is valid, and the latecomers should join the prayer without any additional sermon.
This prevents unnecessary repetition or cancellation of Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو فرغ من الخطبة، فذهبوا كلهم، وجاء آخرون لم يشهدوا الخطبة، فصلى بهم الجمعة: أجزأه.
And if he finishes the khutbah, and then all of them leave, and others come who did not attend the khutbah, and he prays Jumu'ah with them, it suffices him.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This ruling addresses a specific scenario. After the imam completes the two sermons (khutbah), if the entire original congregation departs and a new group arrives who missed the khutbah, the imam may lead them in the two rak'ahs of Jumu'ah. This is valid because the khutbah was performed correctly at its proper time; the new attendees do not need to hear it themselves. The Jumu'ah suffices for both the imam and the new congregation. This illustrates that the khutbah is a condition for the prayer's validity but is an obligation on the community, not on each individual present after the fact.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered by the imam before the Friday prayer, consisting of two parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Pray Zuhr instead
D) Wait for the original congregation to return

Key Takeaway
Once the khutbah is validly delivered, the Jumu'ah prayer is valid even if the congregation changes entirely.
