When Does Going to Jumu'ah Invalidate Dhuhr?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Dhuhr invalidation by Jumu'ah intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on when Dhuhr is invalidated by attending Jumu'ah, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Entering with the imam, not just setting out, is the threshold for Dhuhr's invalidation according to the Sahibayn.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on a key practical question: if a person begins Dhuhr and then decides to attend Jumu'ah, at what point does his Dhuhr become invalid? Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) give different answers, leading to different rulings for someone who changes his mind. The commentator also clarifies a nuance about whether invalidation requires completing Jumu'ah or merely entering with the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling context
The act under discussion is a person who is praying Dhuhr and then sets out (sa'y) to attend the Jumu'ah prayer. The question: when exactly does his Dhuhr prayer become invalid (yantaqid/yaratifid)? Focus on the precise moment of invalidation.
This is a sub-issue of the chapter on Jumu'ah.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
According to Abu Hanifa, the mere act of going to Jumu'ah with the intention of attending invalidates the Dhuhr prayer immediately, even before reaching the mosque or joining the imam.
His view is not explicitly quoted but understood from the Sahibayn's opposition.
3
State the Sahibayn's position (and its transmission variants)
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that Dhuhr is not invalidated until the person enters with the imam (i.e., joins the Jumu'ah prayer). However, the commentator notes a further transmission from Shaykh al-Islam that on their view, invalidation does not occur until the entire Jumu'ah prayer is completed. This disagrees with what is recorded in al-Quduri and al-Hidayah, which only mention entering with the imam.
This shows that even within the Sahibayn's position, there is a subtle difference in how 'entry' is interpreted.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: a person who sets out for Jumu'ah but has not yet entered with the imam can still validly complete his Dhuhr according to the Sahibayn, but according to Abu Hanifa, his Dhuhr is already invalid and he must intend Jumu'ah instead.
This affects real decisions when a person changes their mind.
5
Apply the ruling to the special case of post-imam arrival
The passage clarifies that if the person goes to Jumu'ah after the imam has already prayed (i.e., the Jumu'ah is over), his Dhuhr is not invalidated. This is because the purpose of attending is no longer valid.
This is an exception to the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الجمعة وقالا : لا تبطل صلاة الظهر حتى يدخل مع الإمام . والعبد والمريض والمسافر وغيرهم سواء في الانتقاض بالسعي. كذا في «المصفى». وهذا إذا سعى إليها والإمام في الصلاة، أو قبل أن يصلي، أما إذا سعى إليها وقد صلاها الإمام: لا يبطل ظهره. * قوله : (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : لا تبطل حتى يدخل مع الإمام). فيه إشارة إلى أن الإتمام ليس بشرط لارتفاض الظهر عندهما. وذكر شيخ الإسلام أن على قولهما لا يرتفض ظهره ما لم يؤد الجمعة كلها. وهذا خلاف ما في «القدوري» و«الهداية»)، حيث قالا: لا يبطل حتى يدخل مع الإمام، ولم يقولا : حتى يكملها مع الإمام.
Chapter of Friday Prayer. And they said: Dhuhr prayer is not invalidated until he enters with the imam. And the slave, the sick, the traveler, and others are equal in the invalidation by going. Thus in al-Musaffa. And this is when he goes to it while the imam is in prayer, or before he prays. But if he goes to it and the imam has already prayed, his Dhuhr is not invalidated. * His saying: (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is not invalidated until he enters with the imam.) In this is an indication that completion is not a condition for the invalidation of Dhuhr according to them. And Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that on their view, his Dhuhr is not invalidated as long as he does not perform the entire Jumu'ah. And this is contrary to what is in al-Quduri and al-Hidayah, where they said: It is not invalidated until he enters with the imam, and they did not say: until he completes it with the imam.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding when a person's Dhuhr prayer becomes invalid if he intends to attend Jumu'ah. The commentator begins by citing the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) that Dhuhr is not invalidated merely by setting out for Jumu'ah; rather, it remains valid until the person actually joins the Jumu'ah prayer with the imam (entering with the imam). The commentator then notes that the rule applies equally to all individuals – slave, sick, traveler, etc. He then clarifies that if the person goes while the imam is still praying or before he prays, his Dhuhr is invalid upon joining; but if he goes after the imam has already completed the prayer, his Dhuhr remains valid. The key dispute is about the exact moment of invalidation: Imam Abu Hanifa held that simply setting out with the intention of Jumu'ah invalidates Dhuhr, while the Sahibayn insisted on actual entry with the imam. The commentator quotes an additional nuance from Shaykh al-Islam that according to the Sahibayn, Dhuhr is not invalidated until the person performs the entire Jumu'ah prayer, not just entering. He then contrasts this with what is found in al-Quduri and al-Hidayah, which state only that invalidation occurs upon entering with the imam, not upon completion. This shows a subtle difference in the transmission of the Sahibayn's view.

Key Terms
انتقاض (intiqāḍ): Invalidation of the Dhuhr prayer by the act of going to Jumu'ah.
سعي (sa‘y): The act of going or proceeding to attend the Friday prayer.
ارتفاض (irtifāḍ): Falling away or invalidation of the Dhuhr prayer (used synonymously with intiqāḍ).
دخل مع الإمام (dakhala ma'a al-imam): To enter the Jumu'ah prayer by joining the imam, i.e., starting the prayer with him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the mufta bihi position regarding when Dhuhr is invalidated by attending Jumu'ah?
A) Dhuhr is invalidated immediately upon setting out for Jumu'ah.
B) Dhuhr is invalidated upon entering with the imam.
C) Dhuhr is invalidated only after completing the entire Jumu'ah prayer.
D) Dhuhr is never invalidated; it remains valid regardless.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the mufta bihi position is that a person's Dhuhr prayer becomes invalid upon entering Jumu'ah with the imam, not upon merely setting out.

Villager's Intention and Reward for Jumu'ah
Ruling on reward based on predominant intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the reward for a villager attending Jumu'ah with mixed intentions and identify when the specific reward is earned.

Core Idea
The reward for traveling to Jumu'ah depends on whether worship or worldly need predominates in your intention.

A villager often travels to the city on Friday for multiple purposes: to pray Jumu'ah and to conduct business. Does he earn the reward for going to Jumu'ah? The answer lies in his predominant intention. This lesson unpacks a fatwa from the Hanafi tradition that clarifies this nuance, applying the maxim 'actions are judged by intentions' to a specific scenario of worship and worldly affairs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actor and the action
The fatwa concerns a rustāqī (villager) who travels to the city (miṣr) on Friday. His journey is called 'sa'y' (going). Note that the villager is not obligated to attend Jumu'ah if it is not held in his village, but he may choose to go.
Sa'y here refers to the act of going, not walking quickly.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
The fatwa presents two cases: one where the predominant intention is to perform Jumu'ah, and the other where the predominant intention is to attend to worldly needs (ḥawā'ij). The phrase 'majority of his purpose' is key.
Predominance is based on the strength and priority of the intention, not necessarily on time spent.
3
Determine the ruling for each scenario
If Jumu'ah is the predominant intention, he attains the reward (thawāb) for going to Jumu'ah. If worldly needs are predominant, he does not attain that specific reward, even though his Jumu'ah prayer may be valid.
The reward is for the act of going (sa'y), not for the prayer itself.
4
Connect to the broader principle
This ruling directly applies the ḥadīth 'Innamā al-a'māl bi al-niyyāt' (actions are judged by intentions). The reward for an act of worship is tied to the sincerity and priority of the intention for that worship.
The principle is universal in fiqh, but this fatwa illustrates its application in a mixed-intention scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في «الفتاوى»: الرستاقي إذا سعى يوم الجمعة إلى المصر يريد إقامة الجمعة وإقامة حوائجه، ومعظم مقصوده إقامة الجمعة: ينال ثواب السعي إليها، وإن كان معظم قصده إقامة حوائجه : لا ينال ثواب السعي إلى الجمعة.
He said in al-Fatawa: The villager (rustāqī) when he goes on Friday to the city intending to perform Jumu'ah and to attend to his needs, and his predominant purpose is performing Jumu'ah: he attains the reward of going to it. But if his predominant purpose is attending to his needs: he does not attain the reward of going to Jumu'ah.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage from al-Fatawa addresses the intention of a person from a rural area (rustāqī) who travels to a city on Friday. His journey may have multiple aims: to attend the Jumu'ah prayer and also to take care of personal errands. The ruling depends on which aim is predominant. If his main objective is to perform Jumu'ah, then he earns the reward for travelling to Jumu'ah. However, if his primary intention is to conduct his worldly affairs, and attending Jumu'ah is secondary, then he does not earn that specific reward, though his Jumu'ah prayer itself may be valid. This is a practical application of the principle that actions are judged by intentions, and the reward for acts of worship depends on the sincerity and priority of the intention.

Key Terms
رستاقي (rustāqī): A person living in a rural area or village, as opposed to the city (miṣr).
مصر (miṣr): A large town or city where Jumu'ah is established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The distance he travels.
B) Whether he arrives before the khutbah.
C) His predominant intention in his journey.
D) Whether he performs ablution at home.

Key Takeaway
The reward for going to Jumu'ah is earned only when worship is the predominant intention; worldly aims that dominate nullify this specific reward.

Dislike of Congregational Dhuhr for Excused Persons on Friday
Ruling with commentary expansion on congregational Dhuhr for excused persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational Dhuhr for excused persons on Friday and explain the exceptions for the sick.

Core Idea
Praying Dhuhr in congregation on Friday in the city undermines Jumu'ah – it is disliked, but sick may do so at home.

This passage addresses a subtle fiqh issue: those with excuses from Jumu'ah should not pray Dhuhr in congregation in the city, because it might lead others to abandon Jumu'ah. However, the late Hanafi master al-Tamartashi records an exception from Imam Muhammad for sick individuals praying at home. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its rationale, and the intra-madhhab nuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The base matn states that it is disliked (makruh) for those with excuses (ma'dhurūn) to pray Dhuhr in congregation on Friday in the city (misr). The hukm level is makruh tanzihi.
The city here refers to a place where Jumu'ah is obligatory.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains the reason: it undermines Jumu'ah (ikhlāl bi al-jumu‘a) because others may follow their example and abandon Jumu'ah.
This is a ma'qūl (rational) cause, not a textual one.
3
Examine the extension to prisoners
Prisoners are also subject to the same ruling at first, but then al-Tamartashi quotes Muhammad's distinction: sick are excused, prisoners are not, because prisoners can potentially attend Jumu'ah (by appeasing opponents or seeking help).
The difference is based on capability (qudra).
4
Note the exception for the sick
Imam Muhammad considers it 'hasan' (good) for a sick person to pray Dhuhr in congregation at home with adhan and iqamah. This applies even to a group of sick people.
Exception only applies if the sick are truly incapable; they are not undermining Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* قوله: ( ويكره أن يصلي المعذورون الظهر في جماعة الجمعة يوم في المصر)؛ لما فيه من الإخلال بالجمعة ؛ لأنه قد يقتدي بهم غيرهم. * قوله: (وكذا أهل السجن). قال التمرتاشي: مريض صلى الظهر في منزله يوم الجمعة بأذان وإقامة : قال محمد : هو حسن وكذا جماعة المرضى، بخلاف أهل السجن: فإنه لا يباح لهم ذلك؛ لأن المرضى عاجزون، بخلاف المسجونين؛ لأنهم إذا كانوا ظَلَمةً: قدروا على إرضاء الخصوم، وإن كانوا مظلومين أمكنهم الاستغاثة، وكان عليهم حضور الجمعة.
* His saying: (And it is disliked that those with excuses pray Dhuhr in congregation on Friday in the city) because of the violation of Jumu'ah; for others may follow them. * His saying: (And likewise the prisoners). Al-Tamartashi said: A sick person prayed Dhuhr in his home on Friday with adhan and iqamah: Muhammad said: it is good. And likewise a congregation of sick people, contrary to the prisoners: for it is not permissible for them to do that, because the sick are incapable, unlike the imprisoned; because if they are wrongdoers, they are able to appease their opponents, and if they are wronged, they can seek help, and it is incumbent upon them to attend Jumu'ah.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for individuals who have a valid excuse from attending Jumu'ah (such as illness, travel, etc.). The commentator states that it is makruh (disliked) for such excused persons to pray Dhuhr in congregation in a city on Friday. The reason given is that this practice undermines the institution of Jumu'ah, because others who see them may be misled into thinking that praying Dhuhr in congregation is acceptable on Friday, thereby abandoning Jumu'ah. Then the commentator extends this ruling to prisoners (aḥl al-sijn). However, the discussion from Al-Tamartashi adds nuance: a sick person who prays Dhuhr in his home with adhan and iqamah is considered good according to Imam Muhammad – and similarly a group of sick people may do so. But this is not permissible for prisoners, because the sick are truly incapable of attending Jumu'ah, whereas prisoners are not: if they are unjustly imprisoned, they can seek help (to attend) and if they are justly imprisoned, they can settle their disputes. Thus, prisoners are obliged to attend Jumu'ah if possible, so they may not pray Dhuhr in congregation as a substitute.

Key Terms
معذورون (ma‘dhūrūn): Individuals with a valid excuse (shar‘ī excuse) from attending Jumu'ah, such as illness, travel, or severe weather.
إخلال بالجمعة (ikhlāl bi al-jumu‘a): Undermining or compromising the institution of Friday prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because it leads to neglecting Jumu'ah as others may follow them.
C) Because they must pray only individually and silently.
D) Because they must travel to another city for Jumu'ah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits excused persons from praying Dhuhr in congregation in the city on Friday to protect Jumu'ah, but allows it for the sick at home due to their incapacity.

Dislike of Dhuhr Congregation for Excused Persons on Friday
States the ruling and its rationale, with a distinction between sick and imprisoned.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying Dhuhr in congregation on Friday for those with excuses, explain the rationale, and distinguish the ruling for sick versus imprisoned individuals.

Core Idea
Organizing Dhuhr in congregation on Friday is disliked if it undermines Jumu'ah; exceptions vary by excuse.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding those excused from Jumu'ah. The passage clarifies that even though they are exempt, they should not pray Dhuhr in congregation in the city, lest it detract from the Friday prayer. However, sick people praying at home are distinguished from prisoners, who are still obligated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying Dhuhr in congregation on Friday in a city for those with a valid excuse. The ruling is 'makruh' (disliked).
The text uses 'yukrah' indicating a strong dislike.
2
Understand the rationale
The reason given is 'lama fihi min al-ikhlal bil-jumu'ah' (because of the harm to Jumu'ah) as others may follow and miss the Friday prayer.
This rationale is a qiyas based on the principle of preserving Jumu'ah.
3
Distinguish between sick and prisoners
The sick are 'ajizun (incapable) and may pray Dhuhr in congregation at home (it is 'hasan'). Prisoners are not incapable; Jumu'ah remains obligatory, so it is not permissible for them to pray Dhuhr in congregation.
Al-Timirtashi's report makes this distinction clear.
4
Consider the villager's intention
A villager (rastaqi) traveling to the city: if his main intention is Jumu'ah, he attains reward; if mainly for business, he does not.
This shows that intention affects reward even when the act is the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الجمعة
ويكره أن يصلي المعذورون الظهر بجماعة يوم الجمعة في المصر .
وكذلك أهل السجن .
وهذا خلاف ما في «القدوري» و«الهداية»)، حيث قالا: لا يبطل حتى يدخل مع الإمام، ولم يقولا : حتى يكملها مع الإمام.
قال في «الفتاوى»: الرستاقي إذا سعى يوم الجمعة إلى المصر يريد إقامة الجمعة وإقامة حوائجه، ومعظم مقصوده إقامة الجمعة: ينال ثواب السعي إليها، وإن كان معظم قصده إقامة حوائجه : لا ينال ثواب السعي إلى الجمعة.
* قوله: ( ويكره أن يصلي المعذورون الظهر في جماعة الجمعة يوم في المصر)؛ لما فيه من الإخلال بالجمعة ؛ لأنه قد يقتدي بهم غيرهم. * قوله: (وكذا أهل السجن).
قال التمرتاشي: مريض صلى الظهر في منزله يوم الجمعة بأذان وإقامة : قال محمد : هو حسن وكذا جماعة المرضى، بخلاف أهل السجن: فإنه لا يباح لهم ذلك؛ لأن المرضى عاجزون، بخلاف المسجونين؛ لأنهم إذا كانوا ظَلَمةً: قدروا على إرضاء الخصوم، وإن كانوا مظلومين أمكنهم الاستغاثة، وكان عليهم حضور الجمعة.
Chapter of Friday Prayer. It is disliked that those with excuses pray Dhuhr in congregation on Friday in a city. Likewise the prisoners. And this is contrary to what is in al-Quduri and al-Hidayah, where they said: it is not invalidated until he enters with the imam, and they did not say: until he completes it with the imam. It is said in al-Fatawa: The villager (rastaqi) if he travels on Friday to the city intending to perform Jumu'ah and to fulfill his needs, and most of his intention is to perform Jumu'ah, he attains the reward of traveling to it; but if most of his intention is to fulfill his needs, he does not attain the reward of traveling to Jumu'ah. * His statement: (And it is disliked that those with excuses pray Dhuhr in congregation on Friday in a city) because of the harm to Jumu'ah, for others might follow them. * His statement: (Likewise the prisoners). Al-Timirtashi said: A sick person prays Dhuhr in his home on Friday with adhan and iqamah: Muhammad said: it is good. Likewise a congregation of sick people, contrary to prisoners: for it is not permissible for them; because the sick are incapable, unlike prisoners because if they are oppressors they can appease the opponents, and if they are oppressed, they can seek help, and Jumu'ah attendance is obligatory upon them.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation from the commentator. It begins by stating the ruling: it is disliked (makruh) for those who have a valid excuse (like sickness or travel) to pray Dhuhr in congregation on Friday in a city where Jumu'ah is held. The reason given is that it harms the Friday congregation, as others might follow their example and miss Jumu'ah. This ruling is distinguished from the view of al-Quduri and al-Hidayah, who discussed a different issue—the validity of entering with the imam—and the commentator notes the difference. Then a fatwa is cited about a villager traveling to the city for Jumu'ah: if his main intention is Jumu'ah, he gets the reward; if not, he doesn't. The commentator then elaborates on the ruling, adding that the same applies to prisoners. However, Al-Timirtashi's report distinguishes between sick people and prisoners: sick people may pray Dhuhr in congregation at home, but prisoners cannot, because prisoners are not completely excused—they can either seek justice or reconcile with opponents, so Jumu'ah remains obligatory upon them.

Key Terms
المعذورون (al-ma'dhurūn): Those who have a legitimate shari'i excuse (e.g., sickness, travel) exempting them from Jumu'ah attendance.
الرستاقي (al-rastāqī): A villager or rural dweller living outside the city.
الإخلال بالجمعة (al-ikhlāl bil-jumu'ah): The act of undermining or harming the observance of Friday congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a prisoner who prays Dhuhr in congregation on Friday in a city where Jumu'ah is held?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Disliked (makruh) but not forbidden
C) Forbidden (haram) because Jumu'ah is obligatory upon them
D) Recommended (mandub) like the sick

Key Takeaway
Praying Dhuhr in congregation on Friday in a city is makruh for those excused to avoid harming Jumu'ah; sick people at home are exempted, but prisoners are not.

The Latecomer (Masbuq) in Jumu'ah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the latecomer's obligation in Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the masbuq who catches only the tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw in Jumu'ah, and apply the mufta bihi position to determine whether he prays Jumu'ah or Zuhr.

Core Idea
Catching any part of Jumu'ah suffices for Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Muhammad requires catching most of the second rak'ah.

In Hanafi fiqh, a latecomer (masbuq) who joins the congregation after the prayer has started must complete his prayer according to the imam's prayer. For Jumu'ah, this rule applies, but there is a well-known intra-madhhab difference: how much of the prayer must the latecomer catch to be considered a participant in Jumu'ah? This lesson examines the positions of the three Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the general ruling
The masbuq joins the imam during Jumu'ah and prays whatever he catches, then completes the remainder. The question is whether completing 'as Jumu'ah' or 'as Zuhr' depends on the amount caught.
The matn says 'and builds on it as Jumu'ah' – this is the starting point.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that catching any part, even tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw, suffices to complete as Jumu'ah. Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees.
The commentator explicitly cites the three imams' views.
3
Analyse each imam's reasoning
For Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, 'catching the imam' is fulfilled by any part of the prayer because the prayer is one continuous act. For Muhammad, the essence of Jumu'ah is the two rak'ahs; if one misses most of the second rak'ah, he has not truly participated.
Muhammad's condition: catching most of the second rak'ah (before or during bowing) qualifies as Jumu'ah.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a latecomer catches only the tashahhud, according to the first view he completes two rak'ahs as Jumu'ah; according to Muhammad he must complete four rak'ahs as Zuhr.
The difference is whether the missed portion is made up as Jumu'ah or Zuhr.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The commentator implies the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is relied upon. Later Hanafi scholarship upholds this as the operative position.
The madhhab dispute map shows tarjih in favor of the first view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الجمعة
ومن أدرك الإمام يومَ الجمعة : صلى معه ما أدرك، وبنى عليها
الجمعة .
وإن أدركه في التشهد ، أو في سجود السهو : بنى عليها الجمعة عنـد أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف .
وقال محمد : إن أدرك معه أكثر الركعة الثانية : بنى عليها الجمعة، وإن أدرك أقلها : بنى عليها الظهر.
* قوله : (ومن أدرك الإمام يوم الجمعة صلى معه ما أدرك، وبنى عليها الجمعة).
فإذا قام هذا المسبوق إلى قضائه : كان مخيراً في القراءة: إن شاء جهر، وإن شاء خافت.
قوله: (وإن أدركه في التشهد، أو في سجود السهو: بنى عليها الجمعة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف).
وظاهر هذا: أنه يسجد للسهو في صلاة الجمعة، والمختار عند المتأخرين: أنه لا يسجد في الجمعة والعيدين؛ لتوهم الزيادة من الجهال. * قوله: (وقال محمد: إن أدرك معه أكثر الركعة الثانية: بنى عليها الجمعة)، يعني إذا أدركه قبل أن يركع، أو في الركوع.
قوله: (وإن أدرك أقلها بأن أدركه وقد رفع رأسه من الركوع:
(بنى عليها الظهر)، إلا أنه ينوي الجمعة، إجماعاً.
Chapter of Friday Prayer. And whoever catches the imam on Friday, he prays with him what he catches, and builds on it as Jumu'ah. And if he catches him in the tashahhud or in the prostration of forgetfulness, he builds on it as Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: if he catches with him most of the second rak'ah, he builds on it as Jumu'ah; and if he catches less than that, he builds on it as Zuhr. * His statement: (And whoever catches the imam on Friday, he prays with him what he catches, and builds on it as Jumu'ah). When this latecomer stands to complete his prayer, he has a choice in recitation: if he wishes he may recite aloud, or if he wishes silently. His statement: (And if he catches him in the tashahhud or in the prostration of forgetfulness, he builds on it as Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). The apparent meaning of this is that he performs the prostration of forgetfulness in Jumu'ah prayer, but the chosen position of the later scholars is that he does not prostrate in Jumu'ah and the two Eids, because of the fear of laymen thinking it is an addition. * His statement: (And Muhammad said: if he catches with him most of the second rak'ah, he builds on it as Jumu'ah), meaning if he catches him before he bows or in bowing. His statement: (And if he catches less than that by catching him after he has raised his head from bowing, he builds on it as Zuhr), except that he intends Jumu'ah, by consensus.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the latecomer (masbuq) who joins the Jumu'ah prayer after it has begun. The matn states generally that whoever catches the imam prays what he catches and completes it as Jumu'ah. The commentator expands: the latecomer, when standing to complete his prayer, has the choice to recite aloud or silently. Then the dispute: According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, even if he catches only the tashahhud or the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw), he still completes his prayer as Jumu'ah. But Muhammad al-Shaybani differentiates: if he catches most of the second rak'ah (i.e., before or during bowing), he builds as Jumu'ah; if he catches only a little (after bowing), he must pray the remainder as Zuhr (four rak'ahs), though he intended Jumu'ah. The commentator notes that according to the later scholars, the prostration of forgetfulness is avoided in Jumu'ah and Eid prayers to prevent confusion among the common people. The ruling is that the latecomer must intend Jumu'ah in any case, but if he caught too little, he completes as Zuhr by consensus.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbūq): A latecomer who joins the congregational prayer after it has started, missing one or more rak'ahs.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith (al-tahiyyat) while sitting in the second and fourth rak'ahs.
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a latecomer who catches the imam in the tashahhud of the second rak'ah on Friday?
A) He must complete his prayer as Jumu'ah according to all Hanafi imams.
B) He completes as Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but as Zuhr according to Muhammad.
C) He completes as Zuhr according to all Hanafi imams.
D) He must repeat his prayer because his catching the tashahhud invalidates his Jumu'ah.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position is that catching any part of Jumu'ah, even the tashahhud, suffices to complete the prayer as Jumu'ah, but the minority view of Muhammad requires catching most of the second rak'ah.

Salah — Prayer

Latecomer to Friday Prayer: Catching Tashahhud – Jumu'ah or Zuhr?
Ruling on masbuq in Friday prayer with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on what constitutes 'catching' enough of Friday prayer to build Jumu'ah, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Catching the tashahhud suffices to build Jumu'ah for Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Muhammad requires more than half the second rak'ah.

Being late to Friday prayer raises a critical question: if you join the imam only at the end, can your prayer still count as Jumu'ah? The Hanafi school has a nuanced dispute centred on how much of the prayer you must catch. This lesson unpacks the ikhtilaf between the three eponymous imams and the operative rule for today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Masbuq Scenario
A masbuq is a person who joins the congregation after the imam has started. In Friday prayer, he prays what he catches with the imam and then completes his own prayer. The question is: does his completion count as Jumu'ah (2 rak'ahs) or Zuhr (4 rak'ahs)?
The ruling depends on how much of the congregational prayer he caught.
2
State the Position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They hold that any catching whatsoever is sufficient. If the masbuq catches even the tashahhud (final sitting) or the sajdah al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness), he builds Jumu'ah.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
3
State the Position of Muhammad al-Shaybani
Muhammad differentiates based on the second rak'ah. If the masbuq catches more than half of the second rak'ah (i.e., before or during ruku'), he builds Jumu'ah. If he catches less than half (after ruku'), he builds Zuhr.
Note: Muhammad still requires the initial intention of Jumu'ah by consensus.
4
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The difference affects the number of rak'ahs the masbuq completes after the imam's salam: 2 rak'ahs (Jumu'ah) or 4 rak'ahs (Zuhr). Also, if he catches the tashahhud, under Muhammad's view he would pray 4 rak'ahs of Zuhr, whereas under the other view he prays 2 rak'ahs of Jumu'ah.
This also affects whether he recites aloud or silently in his completion (he has a choice according to the passage).
5
Apply the Mufta Bihi Ruling
The fatwa is based on the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: catching any part, even the tashahhud, allows building Jumu'ah. This is because the congregation is considered a single act of worship, and the imam's prayer encompasses the latecomer.
Later scholars caution against sajdah sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid to avoid confusion, but this does not affect the main ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وإن أدركه في التشهد ، أو في سجود السهو : بنى عليها الجمعة عنـد أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف .
وقال محمد : إن أدرك معه أكثر الركعة الثانية : بنى عليها الجمعة، وإن أدرك أقلها : بنى عليها الظهر.
* قوله : (ومن أدرك الإمام يوم الجمعة صلى معه ما أدرك، وبنى عليها الجمعة).
فإذا قام هذا المسبوق إلى قضائه : كان مخيراً في القراءة: إن شاء جهر، وإن شاء خافت.
قوله: (وإن أدركه في التشهد، أو في سجود السهو: بنى عليها الجمعة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف).
وظاهر هذا: أنه يسجد للسهو في صلاة الجمعة، والمختار عند المتأخرين: أنه لا يسجد في الجمعة والعيدين؛ لتوهم الزيادة من الجهال. * قوله: (وقال محمد: إن أدرك معه أكثر الركعة الثانية: بنى عليها الجمعة)، يعني إذا أدركه قبل أن يركع، أو في الركوع.
قوله: (وإن أدرك أقلها بأن أدركه وقد رفع رأسه من الركوع: (بنى عليها الظهر)، إلا أنه ينوي الجمعة، إجماعاً.
Chapter of Friday Prayer: Whoever catches up with the Imam on Friday prays with him what he caught, and builds Friday prayer upon it. If he catches him in the tashahhud or in the prostration of forgetfulness, he builds Friday prayer upon it according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. So when this latecomer stands to complete what he missed, he has a choice in recitation: if he wishes, he may recite aloud, and if he wishes, silently. His statement: 'If he catches him in the tashahhud or in the prostration of forgetfulness, he builds Friday prayer upon it according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.' Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a latecomer (masbuq) to Friday prayer. The base ruling states that whoever catches the Imam on Friday prays what he caught and then completes the prayer as Jumu'ah. The commentator, Ibn al-Sa'ati, expands on this by noting that when the latecomer stands to finish his prayer, he has the option to recite aloud or silently. The passage then presents a known ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that even if one catches only the tashahhud or the sajdah sahw, he still builds Jumu'ah. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani differentiates based on the second rak'ah: if one catches more than half (i.e., before or during ruku'), he builds Jumu'ah; if less (after ruku'), he builds Zuhr. The commentator adds a later preferred view that sajdah sahw is not performed in Jumu'ah or Eid to avoid confusing laypeople. Finally, it is noted that even when building Zuhr, one must have intended Jumu'ah initially, by consensus.

مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer late and misses some rak'ahs.
التشهد (tashahhud): The final sitting in prayer reciting the testimony of faith.
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness in prayer.

C) Catching the Imam in tashahhud

Key Takeaway
A latecomer to Friday prayer builds Jumu'ah if he catches any part of the congregational prayer per the relied-upon Hanafi view; the minority view of Muhammad requires catching more than half of the second rak'ah.

Forbidden Acts During the Friday Khutbah: Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Ruling on prayer and speech during Friday khutbah with Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) from the Sahibayn's position on conduct during the Friday khutbah and apply the mufta bihi ruling to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
During the Friday khutbah, all talk, prayer, and recitation are prohibited — the Sahibayn allow speech before and after.

When the Imam ascends the minbar for the Friday khutbah, the congregation must cease certain acts to fulfill the obligation of listening. But which acts exactly? The Hanafi school has an internal difference: Imam Abu Hanifa takes the strictest view, prohibiting all speech, prayer, and recitation from the moment the Imam stands until the prayer begins. His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, allow speech before and after the khutbah proper. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each view and establishes the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify the three acts Abu Hanifa prohibits: prayer, speech, and recitation. Note the timing: from when the Imam stands for the khutbah until he finishes.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree on prayer but allow speech before the khutbah begins and after it ends (before the takbir). Their view on recitation is not mentioned here but implied as permissible.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Their proof: the prohibition is tied to the obligation of listening. There is no obligation to listen before the khutbah starts or after it ends, so speech is permitted in those times. Prayer, however, can extend into listening time, so it is prohibited throughout.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa argues that speech can also be prolonged naturally (e.g., a conversation may continue), so it resembles prayer. Therefore, it must be avoided entirely to prevent distraction.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Abu Hanifa, one cannot speak, recite, or pray from the moment the Imam stands until the prayer. According to Sahibayn, one may speak before the khutbah and after it ends (while waiting for the takbir), but not during the khutbah itself.
The mufta bili is Abu Hanifa's view due to precaution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا خرج الإمامُ إلى الخطبة يوم الجمعة : ترك الناسُ الصلاة، والكلام حتى يفرغ من خطبته .
ما يفعله المصلي إذا قام الخطيب إلى المنبر : ]
قوله: (وإذا خرج الإمامُ إلى الخطبة يوم الجمعة)، يعني من المقصورة وظَهَرَ عليهم، فإن لم تكن هناك مقصورة يخرج منها : لم يتركوا القراءة والذكر إلا إذا قام إلى الخطبة.
* قوله : (تَرَكَ الناسُ الصلاة والكلام حتى يفرغ من خطبته).
وكذا القراءة، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة.
وقالا : لا بأس بالكلام قبل أن يخطب، وإذا نزل قبل أن يكبر للإحرام؛ لأن الكراهة للإخلال بفرض الاستماع، ولا استماع في هذين الحالين، بخلاف الصلاة؛ لأنها قد تمتد.
ولأبي حنيفة : أن الكلام أيضاً قد يمتد طبعاً، فأشبه الصلاة. والمراد مطلق الكلام، سواء كان كلام الناس، أو التسبيح، أو تشميت العاطس، أو رد السلام.
وفي «العيون»: المراد به إجابة المؤذن، أما غيره من الكلام: يكره، بالإجماع؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: إذا قلت لصاحبك والإمام يخطب : أنصت: فقد لَغَوْت (۱).
And when the Imam comes out for the khutbah on Friday, the people leave off prayer and speech until he finishes his khutbah. [Heading: What the worshiper does when the preacher stands at the pulpit.] His statement: 'When the Imam comes out for the khutbah on Friday,' meaning from the enclosure and appears before them. If there is no enclosure from which he comes out, they do not leave off recitation and remembrance unless he stands for the khutbah. * His statement: 'The people leave off prayer and speech until he finishes his khutbah.' And likewise recitation, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: There is no harm in speech before he delivers the khutbah, and when he descends before he says the takbir for the prayer, because the prohibition is due to violating the obligation of listening, and there is no listening in these two situations, unlike prayer because it may extend. For Abu Hanifa: Speech also may naturally extend, so it resembles prayer. And the intent is absolute speech, whether it is speech of people, or tasbih, or responding to a sneeze, or returning the greeting. And in al-‘Uyun: The intent is answering the mu’adhdhin; as for other speech, it is disliked by consensus, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'If you say to your companion while the Imam is delivering the khutbah: Listen, you have engaged in laghw (idle talk).'
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding conduct during the Friday khutbah. The basic ruling is that when the Imam emerges for the khutbah, people must cease prayer and speech. The commentator explains that 'coming out' refers to the minbar or enclosure; if no enclosure exists, they only cease when the Imam stands to speak. Abu Hanifa adds that recitation (qira'ah) must also cease, while the two disciples restrict the prohibition to prayer only, allowing speech before the khutbah begins and after it ends (but before the takbir). Their reasoning is that the prohibition is based on listening, which is absent in those times. Abu Hanifa counters that speech can also be prolonged, like prayer, so it must be avoided throughout. The prohibition covers all speech—talking, tasbih, responding to a sneeze, returning salam—but according to al-‘Uyun, the consensus is that answering the mu'adhdhin is also prohibited with karahah, while other speech is makruh. The hadith from Bukhari and Muslim supports the gravity of speaking during the khutbah.

Key Terms
الخطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered before the Friday congregational prayer.
لَغَوْت (laghw): Idle talk that has no benefit; here it refers to speaking during the khutbah, which is sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, which of the following is NOT prohibited during the Friday khutbah?
A) Engaging in conversation
B) Reciting the Quran silently
C) Responding to a sneeze
D) Listening to the khutbah

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi view is that all speech, prayer, and recitation must cease from the moment the Imam stands for the khutbah until the prayer begins.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Prohibition of Speech and Prayer During Friday Khutbah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of prohibition during Friday khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on speech and optional prayer during the Friday khutbah, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the ruling to various scenarios including exceptions.

Core Idea
Any speech or optional worship during the Friday khutbah period is prohibited; even saying 'be quiet' is vain talk.

The Friday khutbah is a condition for Jumu'ah. This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding when exactly speech and prayer become prohibited. By understanding this ruling, you will grasp how the Hanafi school balances the obligation to listen with exceptions for necessity.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling from the matn
Identify the general rule: when the Imam appears for the sermon, people should leave off prayer and speech until he finishes.
The matn says 'When the Imam comes out... leave off prayer and speech.'
2
Identify the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa prohibits all speech and optional prayer from the moment the Imam appears. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) only prohibit during the actual khutbah, permitting speech before and after.
Both agree that supererogatory prayer is prohibited from the Imam's emergence.
3
Understand the proofs of each side
The Sahibayn base their view on the obligation of listening (istima'), which only applies during the khutbah. Abu Hanifa argues that speech, like prayer, can be prolonged and thus distracts.
The hadith about 'Ansiy' supports the general prohibition.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
According to Abu Hanifa, speaking before the khutbah is sinful; Sahibayn permit it. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's stricter view.
In practice, one should remain silent from the Imam's appearance.
5
Recognize exceptions and consensus
Exceptions include warning of danger, making up missed fard prayer, and silently sending blessings on the Prophet. Speech about worldly matters is disliked by consensus.
Even religious conversation is prohibited during the khutbah itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الجمعة
وإذا خرج الإمامُ إلى الخطبة يوم الجمعة : ترك الناسُ الصلاة، والكلام حتى يفرغ من خطبته .
ما يفعله المصلي إذا قام الخطيب إلى المنبر : ]
قوله: (وإذا خرج الإمامُ إلى الخطبة يوم الجمعة)، يعني من المقصورة وظَهَرَ عليهم، فإن لم تكن هناك مقصورة يخرج منها : لم يتركوا القراءة والذكر إلا إذا قام إلى الخطبة.
* قوله : (تَرَكَ الناسُ الصلاة والكلام حتى يفرغ من خطبته).
وكذا القراءة، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة.
وقالا : لا بأس بالكلام قبل أن يخطب، وإذا نزل قبل أن يكبر للإحرام؛ لأن الكراهة للإخلال بفرض الاستماع، ولا استماع في هذين الحالين، بخلاف الصلاة؛ لأنها قد تمتد.
ولأبي حنيفة : أن الكلام أيضاً قد يمتد طبعاً، فأشبه الصلاة. والمراد مطلق الكلام، سواء كان كلام الناس، أو التسبيح، أو تشميت العاطس، أو رد السلام.
وفي «العيون»: المراد به إجابة المؤذن، أما غيره من الكلام: يكره، بالإجماع؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: إذا قلت لصاحبك والإمام يخطب : أنصت: فقد لَغَوْت (۱).
(۱) صحيح البخاري (٩٣٤)، صحيح مسلم (٨٥١).
وروي عن عبد الله بن عمر رضي الله عنهما أنه سمع رجلاً يقول لصاحبه والإمام يخطب : متى تخرج القافلة ؟ فقال له صاحبه: أنصت، فلما فرغ قال للذي قال : أنصت: أما أنت فلا صلاة لك، وأما صاحبك: فحمار).
وقيل: الخلاف في كلام يتعلق بالآخرة أما المتعلق بأمور الدنيا: فمكروه، إجماعاً.
وهذا كله قبل الخطبة، وبعدها، أما فيها : فلا يجوز شيء من الكلام والقراءة والذكر أصلاً؛ لأنه يمنع الاستماع
والمراد من الصلاة التطوع، أما قضاء الفائتة: فيجوز وقت الخطبة من غير كراهة.
ولا يأكل ولا يشرب والإمام يخطب.
وكذا إذا ذكر الخطيب النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: استمعوا، وصلوا عليه في أنفسهم، ولم ينطقوا بها؛ لأنها تُدرك في غير هذه الحال، والسماع يفوت.
فإن رأى رجلاً عند بئر، فخاف وقوعه فيها، أو رأى عقرباً تدبُّ على إنسان: جاز له أن يحذره؛ لأن ذلك يجب لحق آدمي، وهو محتاج إليه، والإنصات لحق الله تعالى، ومبناه على المسامحة؛ لأن الله غني عنه.
(۱) مصنف ابن أبي شيبة (٥٣٤٦)، (٢٦٦٢٧).
Chapter of Friday Prayer
When the Imam comes out for the sermon on Friday, people should leave off prayer and speech until he finishes his sermon.
What the worshiper should do when the preacher stands at the pulpit: ]
His saying: (When the Imam comes out for the sermon on Friday), meaning from the chamber and appears to them. If there is no chamber from which to come out, they do not leave off recitation and remembrance until he stands for the sermon.
* His saying: (People should leave off prayer and speech until he finishes his sermon).
And likewise recitation, and this is according to Abu Hanifa.
They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: There is no harm in speech before he delivers the sermon, and when he descends before he says the opening takbir; because the disapproval is due to violating the duty of listening, and there is no listening in these two situations, unlike prayer because it may be prolonged.
According to Abu Hanifa: Speech may also be prolonged by nature, so it resembles prayer. The intent is absolute speech, whether it is people's speech, tasbih, responding to a sneezer, or returning greetings.
In Al-Uyun: The intent is responding to the mu'adhdhin; as for other speech, it is disliked by consensus, due to his saying, peace be upon him: If you say to your companion while the Imam is delivering the sermon: 'Be quiet,' you have committed a vain act (1).
(1) Sahih al-Bukhari (934), Sahih Muslim (851).
And it is narrated from Abdullah ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, that he heard a man saying to his companion while the Imam was delivering the sermon: 'When will the caravan leave?' So his companion said to him: 'Be quiet.' When he had finished, he said to the one who said 'Be quiet': 'You have no prayer, and as for your companion, he is a donkey.'
It is said: The difference of opinion is concerning speech related to the Hereafter; as for speech related to worldly matters, it is disliked, by consensus.
All this is before and after the sermon; as for during it, nothing of speech, recitation, or remembrance is permissible at all, because it prevents listening.
The intended meaning of prayer is supererogatory prayer; as for making up a missed prayer, it is permissible during the sermon without dislike.
And one should not eat or drink while the Imam is delivering the sermon.
Likewise, if the preacher mentions the Prophet, peace be upon him, they should listen and send blessings upon him in their hearts, and not utter them aloud, because it can be done at other times, and listening is lost.
If he sees a man at a well and fears he might fall into it, or sees a scorpion creeping on a person, it is permissible for him to warn him; because that is obligatory for the right of a human being, and he needs it, while attentive listening is for the right of Allah Almighty, and it is based on leniency; because Allah is independent.
(1) Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba (5346), (26627).
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and ruling update. The commentator expands on the matn from Mukhtasar al-Quduri regarding actions during the Friday khutbah. The base ruling is that when the Imam appears for the sermon, worshipers must cease all optional prayer, recitation (of Quran), and speech until the sermon ends. The clause 'until he finishes' extends the prohibition through the entire sermon, including between the two khutbahs.

Abu Hanifa holds that this prohibition applies from the moment the Imam leaves his chamber (or stands if there is no chamber) until he finishes. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) differentiate: speech is permissible before the Imam begins the khutbah and after he descends before the takbir for prayer, because the obligation to listen only exists during the actual khutbah. However, they agree that prayer (supererogatory) is prohibited from the Imam's emergence because it might lengthen and cause missing part of the khutbah.

Abu Hanifa's counter-argument is that speech can also be prolonged, thus it resembles prayer and should be prohibited. The effective cause (illa) for the prohibition is the need to prevent any distraction from listening to the khutbah, which is a communal obligation.

A hadith from Bukhari and Muslim supports the gravity: even saying 'Ansiy' (be quiet) to someone during the khutbah is considered vain talk (laghw). A narration from Ibn Umar further condemns it, noting that the one who said 'Ansiy' lost his prayer's reward for that Jumu'ah.

The text then resolves to a consensus: speech about worldly matters is disliked (makruh tahriman) during the entire period (before, after, and especially during). Speech about religious matters before and after is permissible but discouraged. During the khutbah itself, all speech, recitation, and even remembrance (dhikr) aloud are absolutely prohibited because they prevent listening.

Exceptions: Making up a missed fard prayer during the khutbah is allowed without dislike, and one may speak to warn of imminent danger (e.g., a well, scorpion) because preserving human life takes priority over listening to the khutbah. Also, when the Prophet (peace be upon him) is mentioned, one should silently invoke blessings without audible speech.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The Friday sermon delivered by the Imam from the minbar before the Jumu'ah prayer.
لغو (laghw): Vain or useless speech that incurs sin, specifically during the Friday khutbah.
استماع (istima'): Attentive listening to the khutbah, which is obligatory during the Friday sermon.
تشميت العاطس (tasmit al-`atis): Responding to a sneeze by saying 'Yarhamuk Allah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, what is the ruling on saying 'Ansiy' (be quiet) to a companion while the Imam is delivering the Friday khutbah?
A) It is permissible because it encourages listening.
B) It is considered vain speech (laghw) and thus prohibited.
C) It is recommended if the companion is talking.
D) It is obligatory to maintain order.

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah demands complete silence from the congregation; even religious speech is prohibited, and the mufta bihi is to cease all speech and optional worship from the moment the Imam appears.
